Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-306 Costs and attorney fees in lien enforcement action.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-306(1): A court entering a judgment or decree in a judicial action brought under this part shall award the prevailing party its costs and reasonable attorney fees incurred before the judgment or decree and, if the association is the prevailing party, any costs and reasonable attorney fees that the association incurs collecting the judgment.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-306(2): In a nonjudicial foreclosure, an association may include in the amount due, and may collect, all costs and reasonable attorney fees incurred in collecting the amount due, including the costs of preparing, recording, and foreclosing a lien.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-307 Action to recover unpaid assessment.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
An association need not pursue a judicial foreclosure or nonjudicial foreclosure to collect an unpaid assessment but may file an action to recover a money judgment for the unpaid assessment without waiving the lien under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-401 Definition.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this part, "reasonably available" means available using typical insurance carriers and markets, irrespective of the ability of the association to pay.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-405 Property insurance.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-405(1): 57-8a-403(1)(a) This section applies to property insurance required under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-405(2): The total amount of coverage provided by blanket property insurance or guaranteed replacement cost insurance may not be less than 100% of the full replacement cost of the insured property at the time the insurance is purchased and at each renewal date, excluding:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-405(2)(a): items normally excluded from property insurance policies; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-405(2)(b): unless otherwise provided in the declaration, any commercial lot in a mixed-use project, including any fixture, improvement, or betterment in a commercial lot in a mixed-use project.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-405(3): Property insurance shall include coverage for any fixture, improvement, or betterment installed at any time to an attached dwelling or to a limited common area appurtenant to a dwelling on a lot, whether installed in the original construction or in any remodel or later alteration, including a floor covering, cabinet, light fixture, electrical fixture, heating or plumbing fixture, paint, wall covering, window, and any other item permanently part of or affixed to an attached dwelling or to a limited common area.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-405(4): Notwithstanding anything in this part and unless otherwise provided in the declaration, an association is not required to obtain property insurance for a loss to a dwelling that is not physically attached to another dwelling or to a common area structure.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-405(5): Each lot owner is an insured person under a property insurance policy.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-405(6): (6)(a); (7) If a loss occurs that is covered by a property insurance policy in the name of an association and another property insurance policy in the name of a lot owner:

Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-405(7)(a): (7); (10) As used in this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-405(7)(a)(i): "Covered loss" means a loss, resulting from a single event or occurrence, that is covered by an association's property insurance policy.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-405(7)(a)(ii): "Lot damage" means damage to any combination of a lot, a dwelling on a lot, or a limited common area appurtenant to a lot or appurtenant to a dwelling on a lot.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-405(7)(a)(iii): "Lot damage percentage" means the percentage of total damage resulting in a covered loss that is attributable to lot damage.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-405(7)(b): A lot owner who owns a lot that has suffered lot damage as part of a covered loss is responsible for an amount calculated by applying the lot damage percentage for that lot to the amount of the deductible under the association's property insurance policy.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-405(7)(c): (7)(b) If a lot owner does not pay the amount required under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-405(8): An association shall set aside an amount equal to the amount of the association's property insurance policy deductible or, if the policy deductible exceeds $10,000, an amount not less than $10,000.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-406 Liability insurance.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-406(1): 57-8a-403(1)(b) This section applies to a liability insurance policy required under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-406(2): A liability insurance policy shall be in an amount determined by the board but not less than an amount specified in the declaration or bylaws.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-406(3): Each lot owner is an insured person under a liability insurance policy that an association obtains, but only for liability arising from:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-406(3)(a): the lot owner's ownership interest in the common areas;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-406(3)(b): maintenance, repair, or replacement of common areas; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-406(3)(c): the lot owner's membership in the association.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407 Damage to a portion of project -- Insurance proceeds.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(1)(a): If a portion of the project for which insurance is required under this part is damaged or destroyed, the association shall repair or replace the portion within a reasonable amount of time unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(1)(a)(i): the project is terminated;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(1)(a)(ii): repair or replacement would be illegal under a state statute or local ordinance governing health or safety; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(1)(a)(iii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(1)(a)(iii)(A): at least 75% of the allocated voting interests of the lot owners in the association vote not to rebuild; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(1)(a)(iii)(B): each owner of a dwelling on a lot and the limited common area appurtenant to that lot that will not be rebuilt votes not to rebuild.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(1)(b): If a portion of a project is not repaired or replaced because the project is terminated, the termination provisions of applicable law and the governing documents apply.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(2)(a): The cost of repair or replacement of any lot in excess of insurance proceeds and reserves is a common expense to the extent the association is required under this chapter to provide insurance coverage for the lot.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(2)(b): The cost of repair or replacement of any common area in excess of insurance proceeds and reserves is a common expense.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(3): If the entire project is damaged or destroyed and not repaired or replaced:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(3)(a): the association shall use the insurance proceeds attributable to the damaged common areas to restore the damaged area to a condition compatible with the remainder of the project;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(3)(b): the association shall distribute the insurance proceeds attributable to lots and common areas that are not rebuilt to:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(3)(b)(i): the lot owners of the lots that are not rebuilt;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(3)(b)(ii): the lot owners of the lots to which those common areas that are not rebuilt were allocated; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(3)(b)(iii): lien holders; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(3)(c): the association shall distribute the remainder of the proceeds to all the lot owners or lien holders in proportion to the common expense liabilities of all the lots.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(4): (4)(a) If the lot owners vote not to rebuild a lot:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(4)(a): the lot's allocated interests are automatically reallocated upon the lot owner's vote as if the lot had been condemned; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-407(4)(b): (4)(a) the association shall prepare, execute, and submit for recording an amendment to the declaration reflecting the reallocations described in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-501 Board.
--------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-501(1): A director shall be:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-501(1)(a): a natural person; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-501(1)(b): 18 years old or older.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-501(2): (1) An association's bylaws may prescribe other qualifications for directors in addition to the requirements described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-501(3): (2) Without limiting the qualifications an association prescribes under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-501(3)(a): has been convicted of a felony; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-501(3)(b): is a sex offender.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-501(4): A director need not be a resident of this state or a unit owner in the association unless required by the association's bylaws.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-501(5): Except as limited in a declaration, the association bylaws, or other provisions of this chapter, a board acts in all instances on behalf of the association.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-502 Period of administrative control.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-502(1): Unless otherwise provided for in a declaration, a period of administrative control terminates on the first to occur of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-502(1)(a): 60 days after 75% of the lots that may be created are conveyed to lot owners other than a declarant;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-502(1)(b): seven years after all declarants have ceased to offer lots for sale in the ordinary course of business; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-502(1)(c): the day the declarant, after giving written notice to the lot owners, records an instrument voluntarily surrendering all rights to control activities of the association.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-502(2): (1); (2)(a); (2)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-502(2)(a): (1) A declarant may voluntarily surrender the right to appoint and remove a member of the board before the period of administrative control terminates under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-502(2)(b): (2)(a) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-502(2)(c): (2)(a) During a period of administrative control, except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-502(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-502(3)(a): Upon termination of the period of administrative control, the lot owners shall elect a board consisting of an odd number of at least three members, a majority of whom shall be lot owners.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-502(3)(b): Unless the declaration provides for the election of officers by the lot owners, the board shall elect officers of the association.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-502(3)(c): The board members and officers shall take office upon election or appointment.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-601 Consolidation of multiple associations.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-601(1): Title 16, Chapter 6a, Part 11, Merger Two or more associations may be consolidated into a single association as provided in
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-601(2): Unless the declaration, articles, or bylaws otherwise provide, a declaration of consolidation between two or more associations to consolidate into a single association is not effective unless it is approved by the lot owners of each of the consolidating associations by the highest percentage of allocated voting interests of the lot owners required by each association to amend its respective declaration, articles, or bylaws.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-601(3): (2) A declaration of consolidation under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-601(3)(a): be prepared, executed, and certified by the president of each of the consolidating associations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-601(3)(b): provide for the reallocation of the allocated interests in the consolidated association by stating:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-601(3)(b)(i): the reallocations of the allocated interests in the consolidated association or the formulas used to reallocate the allocated interests; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-601(3)(b)(ii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-601(3)(b)(ii)(A): the percentage of overall allocated interests of the consolidated association that are allocated to all of the lots comprising each of the consolidating associations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-601(3)(b)(ii)(B): that the portion of the percentages allocated to each lot formerly comprising a part of a consolidating association is equal to the percentages of allocated interests allocated to the lot by the declaration of the consolidating association.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-601(4): (2) A declaration of consolidation under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-601(5): Unless otherwise provided in the declaration of consolidation:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-601(5)(a): the consolidated association resulting from a consolidation under this section is the legal successor for all purposes of all of the consolidating associations;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-601(5)(b): the operations and activities of all of the consolidating associations shall be consolidated into the consolidated association; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-601(5)(c): the consolidated association holds all powers, rights, obligations, assets, and liabilities of all consolidating associations.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701 Solar energy system -- Prohibition or restriction in declaration or association rule.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(1): As used in this section, "detached dwelling" means a detached dwelling for which the association does not have an ownership interest in the detached dwelling's roof.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(2)(a): A governing document other than a declaration may not prohibit an owner of a lot with:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(2)(a)(i): a detached dwelling from installing a solar energy system; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(2)(a)(ii): a dwelling attached to other dwellings from installing a solar energy system, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(2)(a)(ii)(A): the association does not have an ownership interest in the dwelling's roof or building exterior;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(2)(a)(ii)(B): the association does not have a maintenance, repair, or replacement obligation in the dwelling's roof or building exterior; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(2)(a)(ii)(C): all lot owners with attached dwellings in the building agree to the installation of the solar energy system.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(2)(b): A governing document other than a declaration or an association rule may not restrict an owner of a lot with:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(2)(b)(i): a detached dwelling from installing a solar energy system on the owner's lot; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(2)(b)(ii): a dwelling attached to other dwellings from installing a solar energy system on the roof of the dwelling's building, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(2)(b)(ii)(A): the association does not have an ownership interest in the dwelling's roof or building exterior;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(2)(b)(ii)(B): the association does not have a maintenance, repair, or replacement obligation in the dwelling's roof or building exterior; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(2)(b)(ii)(C): all lot owners with attached dwellings in the building agree to the installation of the solar energy system.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(3): (6) A declaration may, for a lot with a detached dwelling:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(3)(a): prohibit a lot owner from installing a solar energy system; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(3)(b): (6) impose a restriction other than a prohibition on a solar energy system's size, location, or manner of placement if the restriction:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(3)(b)(i): decreases the solar energy system's production by 5% or less;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(3)(b)(ii): increases the solar energy system's cost of installation by 5% or less; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(3)(b)(iii): (6) complies with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(4)(a): If a declaration does not expressly prohibit the installation of a solar energy system on a lot with a detached dwelling, an association may not amend the declaration to impose a prohibition on the installation of a solar energy system unless the association approves the prohibition by a vote of greater than 67% of the allocated voting interests of the lot owners in the association.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(4)(b): An association may amend an existing provision in a declaration that prohibits the installation of a solar energy system on a lot with a detached dwelling if the association approves the amendment by a vote of greater than 67% of the allocated voting interests of the lot owners in the association.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(5): (6) An association may, by association rule, for a lot with a detached dwelling, impose a restriction other than a prohibition on a lot owner's installation of a solar energy system if the restriction:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(5)(a): (6) complies with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(5)(b): decreases the solar energy system's production by 5% or less; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(5)(c): increases the solar energy system's cost of installation by 5% or less.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6): A declaration or an association rule may require an owner of a dwelling that installs a solar energy system on the owner's lot:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6)(a): to install a solar energy system that, or install the solar energy system in a manner that:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6)(a)(i): complies with applicable health, safety, and building requirements established by the state or a political subdivision of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6)(a)(ii): if the solar energy system is used to heat water, is certified by:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6)(a)(ii)(A): the Solar Rating and Certification Corporation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6)(a)(ii)(B): a nationally recognized solar certification entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6)(a)(iii): if the solar energy system is used to produce electricity, complies with applicable safety and performance standards established by:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6)(a)(iii)(A): the National Electric Code;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6)(a)(iii)(B): the Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6)(a)(iii)(C): Underwriters Laboratories;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6)(a)(iii)(D): an accredited electrical testing laboratory; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6)(a)(iii)(E): the state or a political subdivision of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6)(a)(iv): if the solar energy system is mounted on a roof:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6)(a)(iv)(A): does not extend above the roof line; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6)(a)(iv)(B): has panel frame, support bracket, or visible piping or wiring that has a color or texture that is similar to the roof material; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6)(a)(v): if the solar energy system is mounted on the ground, is not visible from the street that a lot fronts;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6)(b): to pay any reasonable cost or expense incurred by the association to review an application to install a solar energy system;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6)(c): be responsible, jointly and severally with any subsequent owner of the lot while the violation of the rule or requirement occurs, for any cost or expense incurred by the association to enforce a declaration requirement or association rule; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-701(6)(d): as a condition of installing a solar energy system, to record a deed restriction against the owner's lot that runs with the land that requires the current owner of the lot to indemnify or reimburse the association or a member of the association for any loss or damage caused by the installation, maintenance, or use of the solar energy system, including costs and reasonable attorney fees incurred by the association or a member of the association.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-702 Attorney fees.
----------------------------------------------
In an action to enforce this part, the court may award the prevailing party, in addition to any other available relief, an amount equal to the prevailing party's costs and reasonable attorney fees.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-703 Applicability.
----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-703(1): (2) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-703(2): This part does not apply to an express prohibition or an express restriction on a lot owner's installation of a solar energy system:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-703(2)(a): described in a declaration recorded before January 1, 2017; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-703(2)(b): created by official association action taken before January 1, 2017.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-703(3): This part does not apply during the period of administrative control.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-801 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-801(1): "Charging system" means a device that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-801(1)(a): used to provide electricity to an electric or hybrid electric vehicle; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-801(1)(b): designed to ensure a safe connection between the electric grid and the vehicle.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-801(2): 58-55-102 "General electrical contractor" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-801(3): 58-55-102 "Residential electrical contractor" means the same as that term is defined in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802 Electric vehicle charging systems -- Restrictions -- Responsibilities.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(1): Notwithstanding any provision in an association's governing documents to the contrary, an association may not prohibit a lot owner from installing or using a charging system in:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(1)(a): a parking space:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(1)(a)(i): on the lot owner's lot; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(1)(a)(ii): used for the parking or storage of a vehicle or equipment; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(1)(b): a limited common area parking space designated for the lot owner's exclusive use.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(2): An association may:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(2)(a): require a lot owner to submit an application for approval of the installation of a charging system;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(2)(b): require the lot owner to agree in writing to:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(2)(b)(i): hire a general electrical contractor or residential electrical contractor to install the charging system; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(2)(b)(ii): if a charging system is installed in a common area, provide reimbursement to the association for the actual cost of the increase in the association's insurance premium attributable to the installation or use of the charging system;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(2)(c): require a charging system to comply with:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(2)(c)(i): the association's reasonable design criteria governing the dimensions, placement, or external appearance of the charging system; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(2)(c)(ii): applicable building codes;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(2)(d): impose a reasonable charge to cover costs associated with the review and permitting of a charging system;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(2)(e): impose a reasonable restriction on the installation and use of a charging system that does not significantly:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(2)(e)(i): increase the cost of the charging system; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(2)(e)(ii): decrease the efficiency or performance of the charging system; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(2)(f): require a lot owner to pay the costs associated with installation, metering, and use of the charging system, including the cost of:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(2)(f)(i): electricity associated with the charging system; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(2)(f)(ii): damage to a general common area, a limited common area, or an area subject to the exclusive use of another lot owner that results from the installation, use, maintenance, repair, removal, or replacement of the charging system.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(3): A lot owner who installs a charging system shall disclose to a prospective buyer of the lot:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(3)(a): the existence of the charging system; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(3)(b): the lot owner's related responsibilities under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(4): Unless the lot owner and the association or the declarant otherwise agree:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(4)(a): a charging system installed under this section is the personal property of the lot owner of the lot with which the charging system is associated; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(4)(b): a lot owner who installs a charging system shall, before transferring ownership of the owner's lot, unless the prospective buyer of the lot accepts ownership and all rights and responsibilities that apply to the charging system under this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(4)(b)(i): remove the charging system; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-8a-802(4)(b)(ii): restore the premises to the condition before installation of the charging system.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 57 - Chapter 9 - Marketable Record Title
********************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-1 What constitutes marketable record title.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Any person having the legal capacity to own land in this state, who has an unbroken chain of title of record to any interest in land for 40 years or more, shall be deemed to have a marketable record title to such interest as defined in SectionUtah Code Annotated § 57-9-1(1): the person claiming such interest or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-1(2): some other person from whom, by one or more conveyances or other title transactions of record, such purported interest has become vested in the person claiming such interest: with nothing appearing of record, in either case, purporting to divest such claimant of such purported interest.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-2 Rights and interests to which marketable record title is subject.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The marketable record title is subject to:Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-2(1): all interests and defects which are inherent in the muniments of which such chain of record title is formed, except that a general reference in the muniments or any of them, to easements, use restrictions, or other interests created prior to the root of title is not sufficient to preserve them, unless specific identification is made therein of a recorded title transaction which creates  the easement, use restriction, or other interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-2(2): 57-9-4 all interests preserved by the filing of proper notice or by possession by the same owner continuously for a period of 40 years or more, in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-2(3): the rights of any person arising from prescriptive use or a period of adverse possession or user, which was in whole or in part subsequent to the effective date of the root of title;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-2(4): 57-9-3 any interest arising out of a title transaction which has been recorded subsequent to the effective date of the root of title from which the unbroken chain of title of record is started, except that the recording does not revive or give validity to any interest which has been extinguished prior to the time of the recording by the operation of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-2(5): 57-9-6 the exceptions stated in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-3 Marketable record title held free and clear of interests, claims, and charges.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Subject to SectionsUtah Code Annotated § 57-9-3(1): the marketable record title shall be held by its owner and shall be taken by any person dealing with the land free and clear of all interests, claims, or charges, whatsoever, the existence of which depends upon any act, transaction, event, or omission that occurred prior to the effective date of the root of title; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-3(2): all such interests, claims, or charges, however denominated, whether legal or equitable, present or future, whether the interests, claims, or charges are asserted by a person sui juris or under a disability, whether the person is within or without the state, whether the person is natural or corporate, or is private or governmental, are declared to be void.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-4 Filing of notice of claim of interest authorized -- Effect of possession of land by record owner of possessory interest.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-4(1): Any person claiming an interest in land may preserve and keep effective such interest by filing for record during the forty-year period immediately following the effective date of the root of title of the person whose record title would otherwise be marketable, a notice in writing, duly verified by oath, setting forth the nature of the claim. No disability or lack of knowledge of any kind on the part of anyone shall suspend the running of the forty-year period. The notice may be filed for record by the claimant or by any other person acting in behalf of any claimant who is
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-4(1)(a): under a disability,
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-4(1)(b): unable to assert a claim on his own behalf, or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-4(1)(c): one of a class, but whose identity cannot be established or is uncertain at the time of filing the notice of claim for record.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-4(2): (1); (1) If the same record owner of any possessory interest in land has been in possession of such land continuously for a period of 40 years or more, during which period no title transaction with respect to such interest appears of record in his chain of title, and no notice has been filed by him or on his behalf as provided in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-5 Notice of claim of interest -- Contents -- Filing for record.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
In order to be effective and to be recorded, the notice required by Section

Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-6 Applicability of provisions.
---------------------------------------------------------
This chapter may not be applied to:Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-6(1): bar a lessor or the lessor's successor as a reversioner of the right to possession on the expiration of any lease;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-6(2): extinguish any right, title, or interest created or held for any pipeline, highway, railroad or public utility purpose;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-6(3): extinguish an easement or interest in the nature of an easement, the existence of which is clearly observable by physical evidence of its use;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-6(4): extinguish any water rights, whether evidenced by decrees, by certificates of appropriation, by diligence claims to the use of surface or underground water, or by water users' claims filed in general determination proceedings;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-6(5): extinguish any right, title, estate, or interest in and to minerals, and any development, mining, production or other rights or easements related to the minerals or exercisable in connection  with the minerals;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-6(6): extinguish  any right, title, or interest of the state or political subdivision of the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-6(7): extinguish any right, title, or interest of the United States, by reason of failure to file the notice required under this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-7 Existing statutes of limitations and recording statutes not affected.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Nothing contained in this act shall be construed to extend the period for the bringing of an action or for the doing of any other required act under any statutes of limitations, nor, except as herein specifically provided, to affect the operation of any statutes governing the effect of the recording or the failure to record any instrument affecting land.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-8 Definitions.
-----------------------------------------
As used in this act:Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-8(1): 57-9-1; 57-9-3 The words "marketable record title" mean a title of record as indicated in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-8(2): The word "records" includes probate and other official public records, as well as records in the registry of deeds.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-8(3): The word "recording," when applied to the official public records of a probate or other court, includes filing.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-8(4): The words "person dealing with land" include a purchaser of any estate or interest therein, a mortgagee, a levying or attaching creditor, a land contract vendee, or any other person seeking to acquire an estate or interest therein, or impose a lien thereon.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-8(5): The words "root of title" mean that conveyance or other title transaction in the chain of title of a person, purporting to create the interest claimed by such person, upon which he relies as a basis for the marketability of his title, and which was the most recent to be recorded as of a date 40 years prior to the time when marketability is being determined. The effective date of the "root of title" is the date on which it is recorded.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-8(6): The words "title transaction" mean any transaction affecting title to any interest in land, including title by will or descent, title by tax deed, or by trustee's, referee's, guardian's, executor's, administrator's, master in chancery's, or sheriff's deed, or decree of any court, as well as warranty deed, quitclaim deed, or mortgage.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-9 Legislative purpose and construction.
------------------------------------------------------------------
This act shall be liberally construed to effect the legislative purpose of simplifying and facilitating land title transactions by allowing persons to rely on a record chain of title as described in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 57-9-10 Extension of limitation period.
-------------------------------------------------------------
If the forty-year period specified in this act shall have expired prior to two years after the effective date of this act, such period shall be extended two years after the effective date of this act.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 57 - Chapter 10 - Utah Coordinate System
********************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-1 Plane coordinate systems designated -- Zones within the systems by county.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-1(1): The systems of plane coordinates that have been established by the National Ocean Service/National Geodetic Survey (formerly the United States Coast and Geodetic Survey) or its successors for defining and stating the geographic positions or locations of points on the surface of the earth within the state of Utah are known and designated as the Utah Coordinate System of 1927 and the Utah Coordinate System of 1983.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-1(2): For the purpose of the use of these systems, the state is divided into three zones: North, Central, and South Zones.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-1(2)(a): The area now included in the following counties constitutes the North Zone: Box Elder, Cache, Daggett, Davis, Morgan, Rich, Summit, and Weber.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-1(2)(b): The area now included in the following counties constitutes the Central Zone: Carbon, Duchesne, Emery, Grand, Juab, Millard, Salt Lake, Sanpete, Sevier, Tooele, Uintah, Utah, and Wasatch.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-1(2)(c): The area now included in the following counties constitutes the South Zone: Beaver, Garfield, Iron, Kane, Piute, San Juan, Washington, and Wayne.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-2 Zones must be named in maps and documents.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-2(1): As established for use in the North Zone, the Utah Coordinate System of 1927 or the Utah Coordinate System of 1983 shall be named and designated as the "Utah Coordinate System 1927 North Zone" or "Utah Coordinate System 1983 North Zone" in any land description or on any map or document in which it is used.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-2(2): As established for use in the Central Zone, the Utah Coordinate System of 1927 or the Utah Coordinate System of 1983 shall be named and designated as the "Utah Coordinate System 1927 Central Zone" or "Utah Coordinate System 1983 Central Zone" in any land description or on any map or document in which it is used.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-2(3): As established for use in the South Zone, the Utah Coordinate System of 1927 or the Utah Coordinate System of 1983 shall be named and designated as the "Utah Coordinate System 1927 South Zone" or "Utah Coordinate System 1983 South Zone" in any land description or on any map or document in which it is used.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-3 North to South and East to West coordinate values.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The plane coordinate values for a point on the earth's surface used to express the geographic position or location or point in the appropriate zone of this system shall consist of two distances expressed in U.S. survey feet and decimals of a foot when using the Utah Coordinate System of 1927 and expressed in meters and decimals of a meter when using the Utah Coordinate System of 1983.Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-3(1): One of these distances, known as the "x-coordinate" or "E-coordinate," shall give the position in an east-west direction; the other, known as the "y-coordinate" or "N-coordinate," shall give the position in a north-south direction.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-3(2): These coordinates shall be made to depend upon and conform to plane rectangular coordinate values computed on the systems defined in this chapter for the monumented points of the North American Horizontal Geodetic Control Network, as published by the National Ocean Service/National Geodetic Survey (formerly the United States Coast and Geodetic Survey) or its successors.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-3(3): Any such station may be used for establishing a survey connection to either Utah coordinate system.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-4 Legal effect of descriptions using coordinate values.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-4(1): A description of the location of any survey station or land boundary corner in the state is complete, legal, and satisfactory if it is expressed by use of the system of plane coordinates defined in this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-4(2): For purposes of sale or title transfer, no real property may be described solely by reference to coordinate values from the Utah coordinate system or any other coordinate system.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-4(3): When coordinates based on the Utah coordinate system are used in the description of any tract of land, they are supplemental to the basic description relating to existing recognized monuments and land lines of record.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-4(4): The description by reference to the subdivision, line, or corner of the United States public land surveys prevails over the description by coordinates, if there is any conflict between the descriptions.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-5 Descriptions of tracts extending over more than one zone.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-5(1): When any tract of land that is to be defined by a single land description extends from one into another of the coordinate zones, the positions of all points on its boundaries may be referred to by either of the two zones.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-5(2): The zone that is used shall be identified specifically in the land description.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6 Utah Coordinate Systems of 1927 and 1983 defined.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
For purposes of more precisely defining the Utah Coordinate Systems, the following special publications are adopted:Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(1): For the Utah Coordinate System of 1927, the manual entitled "The State Coordinate Systems (A Manual for Surveyors)," Special Publication No. 235, and "Plane Coordinate Projection Tables for Utah," Special Publication No. 277.  Both manuals are published by the U.S. Department of Commerce, Coast and Geodetic Survey, and provide, in part, the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(1)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(1)(a)(i): The "Utah Coordinate System of 1927 North Zone" is a Lambert Conformal Conic Projection of the Clarke Spheroid of 1866 having standard parallels at north latitudes 41 degrees 47 minutes and 40 degrees 43 minutes, along which parallels the scale shall be exact.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(1)(a)(ii): The origin of coordinates is at the intersection of the meridian 111 degrees 30 minutes west of Greenwich and the parallel 40 degrees 20 minutes north latitude.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(1)(a)(iii): This origin is given the coordinates: x=2,000,000 feet and y=0 feet.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(1)(b)(i): The "Utah Coordinate System of 1927 Central Zone" is a Lambert Conformal Conic Projection of the Clarke Spheroid of 1866 having standard parallels at north latitudes 40 degrees 39 minutes and 39 degrees 01 minutes, along which parallels the scale shall be exact.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(1)(b)(ii): The origin of coordinates is at the intersection of the meridian 111 degrees 30 minutes west of Greenwich and the parallel 38 degrees 20 minutes north latitude.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(1)(b)(iii): This origin is given the coordinates: x=2,000,000 feet and y=0 feet.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(1)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(1)(c)(i): The "Utah Coordinate System of 1927 South Zone" is a Lambert Conformal Conic Projection of the Clarke Spheroid of 1866 having standard parallels at north latitudes 38 degrees 21 minutes and 37 degrees 13 minutes, along which parallels the scale shall be exact.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(1)(c)(ii): The origin of coordinates is at the intersection of the meridian 111 degrees 30 minutes west of Greenwich and the parallel 36 degrees 40 minutes north latitude.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(1)(c)(iii): This origin is given the coordinates: x=2,000,000 feet and y=0 feet.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(2): For the Utah Coordinate System of 1983, the manual entitled "State Plan Coordinate System of 1983," NOAA Manual NOS NGS 5.  The manual is published by the U.S. Department of Commerce, National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration, and provides, in part, the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(2)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(2)(a)(i): The "Utah Coordinate System of 1983 North Zone" is a Lambert Conformal Conic Projection of the North American Datum of 1983 having standard parallels at north latitudes 41 degrees 47 minutes and 40 degrees 43 minutes, along which parallels the scale shall be exact.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(2)(a)(ii): The origin of coordinates is at the intersection of the meridian 111 degrees 30 minutes west of Greenwich and the parallel 40 degrees 20 minutes north latitude.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(2)(a)(iii): This origin is given the coordinates: x or E=500,000 meters and y or N=1,000,000 meters.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(2)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(2)(b)(i): The "Utah Coordinate System of 1983 Central Zone" is a Lambert Conformal Conic Projection of the North American Datum of 1983 having standard parallels at north latitudes 40 degrees 39 minutes and 39 degrees 01 minutes, along which parallels the scale shall be exact.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(2)(b)(ii): The origin of coordinates is at the intersection of the meridian 111 degrees 30 minutes west Greenwich and the parallel 38 degrees 20 minutes north latitude.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(2)(b)(iii): This origin is given the coordinates: x or E=500,000 meters and y or N=2,000,000 meters.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(2)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(2)(c)(i): The "Utah Coordinate System of 1983 South Zone" is a Lambert Conformal Conic Projection of the North American Datum of 1983 having standard parallels at north latitudes 38 degrees 21 minutes and 37 degrees 13 minutes, along which parallels the scale shall be exact.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(2)(c)(ii): The origin of coordinates is at the intersection of the meridian 111 degrees 30 minutes west of Greenwich and the parallel 36 degrees 40 minutes north latitude.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-6(2)(c)(iii): This origin is given the coordinates: x or E=500,000 meters and y or N=3,000,000 meters.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-7 Coordinates required to be based on control stations.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-7(1): Coordinates based on either the Utah Coordinate System of 1927 or the Utah Coordinate System of 1983 that purport to define the position of a point on a land boundary shall be based on a monumented horizontal control station established in conformity with the standards of accuracy and specifications for first or second order geodetic surveying, as prepared and published by the Federal Geodetic Control Committee (FGCC) of the United States Department of Commerce.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-7(1)(a): Standards and specifications of the FGCC or its successor in force on the date of the survey shall apply.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-7(1)(b): Publishing existing control stations, or the acceptance with intent to publish the newly established stations, by the National Ocean Service/National Geodetic Survey constitutes evidence of adherence to the FGCC specifications.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-7(2): 57-10-6 Control stations which have been established by agencies of the state or its political subdivisions may also be used, provided those points are established in conformity with the standards set forth in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-8 Use of terms on maps and documents.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-8(1): 57-10-9; 57-10-6(1); 57-10-6(2) Any document identifying or using a coordinate system shall, in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-8(1)(a): 57-10-6(1) The use of the term "Utah Coordinate System of 1927 (North, Central, South) Zone" on any map, report of survey, or other document shall be used to reference the system, the coordinates, and the unit of measure as defined in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-8(1)(b): 57-10-6(2) The use of the term "Utah Coordinate System of 1983 (HARN 1994, or the current federal coordinate update used as the basis of the system being used) (North, Central, South) Zone" shall be used to reference the system, the coordinates, and the unit of measure as defined in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-8(2): Anyone using a coordinate system similar to the Utah coordinate system, such as one where a modified elevation datum is used, shall clearly include "modified" in the title of the coordinate system.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-8(3): Any survey or map based on any such modified coordinate system shall show the title of the coordinate system, including "modified" in the title and show the appropriate combined adjustment factor relating the system to the Utah coordinate system.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-9 Use of coordinate system optional.
----------------------------------------------------------------
The use of the Utah coordinate system by any person, corporation, or governmental agency engaged in land surveying or mapping, or both, is optional.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-10-11 Requirement to conform to the Utah Coordinate System.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A person, corporation, municipality, county, or state agency that is utilizing an existing county coordinate system or establishing a new countywide coordinate network for surveying or mapping, or both,  shall, by January 1, 2021,  conform to the current Utah Coordinate System, along with the current federal coordinate update.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 57 - Chapter 11 - Utah Uniform Land Sales Practices Act
***********************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-1 Short title.
------------------------------------------
This act shall be known and may be cited as the "Utah Uniform Land Sales Practices Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2 Definitions.
------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(1)(a): "Disposition" includes sale, lease, assignment, award by lottery, or any other transaction concerning a subdivision, if undertaken for gain or profit.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(1)(b): "Disposition" does not include the sale or lease of land held by railroads for right of way if the land is within 400 feet of the center line of a railroad tract.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(2): 61-2-201 "Division" means the Division of Real Estate created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(3): "Federal act" means the federal Interstate Land Sales Full Disclosure Act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 1701, et seq., or any successor federal act.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(4)(a): "Industrial park" means a subdivision or subdivided lands offered as a part of a common promotional plan of advertising and sale zoned for office, manufacturing, warehousing, commercial, industrial, distribution, or wholesale use and utilized for one or more of those purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(4)(b): "Industrial park" does not include land offered for sale that is designed or intended to be used for recreational, residential, including multiple family dwellings, or agricultural purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(5): "Offer" includes an inducement, solicitation, or attempt to encourage a person to acquire an interest in land if undertaken for gain or profit.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(6): "Person" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(6)(a): a business trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(6)(b): an estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(6)(c): a trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(6)(d): a partnership;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(6)(e): an unincorporated association;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(6)(f): two or more of any entity having a joint or common interest; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(6)(g): any other legal or commercial entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(7): "Purchaser" means a person who acquires or attempts to acquire or succeeds to an interest in land.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(8): "Residential building" means a structure intended for occupation as a residence which, at the time of an offer or disposition of the unit on which it is situated, or on which there is a legal obligation on the part of the seller to complete construction of it within two years from date of disposition, has, or if completed would have, ready access to water, gas, electricity, and roads.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(9): "Subdivider" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(9)(a): an owner of an interest in subdivided lands who offers the subdivided lands for disposition; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(9)(b): a principal agent of an owner of an interest in subdivided lands if the owner is inactive.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(10): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(10)(a): "Subdivision" and "subdivided lands" means land that is divided or is proposed to be divided for the purpose of disposition into 10 or more units including land, whether contiguous or not, if 10 or more units are offered as a part of a common promotional plan of advertising and sale.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(10)(b): If a subdivision is offered by a developer or group of developers, and the land is contiguous or is known, designated, or advertised as a common tract or by a common name, that land is presumed, without regard to the number of units covered by each individual offering, to be part of a common promotional plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-2(11): "Unit" includes a lot, parcel, or other interest in land separately offered for disposition.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-3 Administration by division.
---------------------------------------------------------
The division shall administer this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-5 Registration, public offering statement, and receipt required for sale of subdivided land -- Temporary permit -- Right of rescission.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-5(2)(c): provide evidence acceptable to the division that all funds received by the developer or marketing agent will be placed into an independent escrow with instructions that funds will not be released until a final registration has been granted;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-5(2)(d): give to each purchaser and potential purchaser a copy of the proposed property report which the developer has submitted to the division with the original application; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-5(2)(e): give to each purchaser the opportunity to rescind the purchase in accordance with this section.  The purchaser must be granted an additional opportunity to rescind upon the issuance of an approved registration if the division determines that there is a substantial difference in the disclosures contained in the final property report and those given to the purchaser in the proposed property report.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-5(3): Any contract or agreement of disposition for an interest in subdivided lands may be rescinded by the purchaser without cause by midnight of the fifth calendar day after the execution of the contract or agreement of disposition.  This right of rescission may not be waived by agreement.  The contract or agreement of disposition shall state in boldface type on the signature page above all signatures: YOU HAVE THE OPTION TO CANCEL YOUR CONTRACT OR AGREEMENT OF DISPOSITION BY NOTICE TO THE SELLER UNTIL MIDNIGHT OF THE FIFTH CALENDAR DAY FOLLOWING THE SIGNING OF THE CONTRACT OR AGREEMENT.  WRITTEN NOTICE OF CANCELLATION MUST BE PERSONALLY DELIVERED OR SENT BY CERTIFIED MAIL, POSTMARKED BY MIDNIGHT OF THE FIFTH CALENDAR DAY FOLLOWING THE SIGNING OF THE CONTRACT OR AGREEMENT, TO THE SELLER AT: (Address of Seller).
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-5(4): 57-11-17; 57-11-13; 57-11-14 No person may dispose of any interest in subdivided lands without delivering to the purchaser an effective, current public offering statement and obtaining a dated, signed receipt for the public offering statement in a form to be approved by the division from each purchaser.  The subdivider shall retain each receipt for two years from the date of its execution.  All receipts shall be made available for inspection upon request by the division.  Failure to comply with this subsection shall not constitute a cause of action under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-6(1)(k): if there is a lien or encumbrance affecting more than one unit, a statement of the consequences to a purchaser of failure to discharge the lien or encumbrance and the steps, if any, taken to protect the purchaser in case of this eventuality;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-6(1)(l): copies of instruments creating easements, restrictions, or other encumbrances affecting the subdivided lands;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-6(1)(m): a statement of the zoning and other governmental regulations affecting the use of the subdivided lands and of any existing or proposed taxes or special assessments which affect the subdivided lands;

Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7 Public offering statement -- Contents -- Restrictions on use -- Alteration or amendments.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(1): Every public offering statement shall disclose completely and accurately to prospective purchasers:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(1)(a): the physical characteristics of the subdivided lands offered; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(1)(b): unusual and material circumstances or features affecting the subdivided lands.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(2): (2)(e)(i); (ii); (2)(f)(i) The proposed public offering statement submitted to the division shall be in a form prescribed by its rules and, unless otherwise provided by the division, shall include the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(2)(a): the name and principal address of the subdivider and the name and principal address of each officer, director, general partner, other principal, or person occupying a similar status or performing similar functions as defined by the rules of the division if the subdivider is a person other than an individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(2)(b): a general description of the subdivided lands stating the total number of units in the offering;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(2)(c): a statement summarizing in one place the significant terms of any encumbrances, easements, liens, severed interests, and restrictions, including zoning and other regulations affecting the subdivided lands and each unit, and a statement of all existing or proposed taxes or special assessments which affect the subdivided lands;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(2)(d): a statement of the use for which the property is offered;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(2)(e): (2)(e)(i); (ii) information concerning:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(2)(e)(i): any improvements, including streets, curbs, and gutters, sidewalks, water supply including a supply of culinary water, drainage and flood control systems, irrigation systems, sewage disposal facilities, and customary utilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(2)(e)(ii): the estimated cost to the purchaser, the estimated date of completion, and the responsibility for construction and maintenance of existing and proposed improvements which are referred to in connection with the offering or disposition; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(2)(e)(iii): (2)(e)(i); (ii) if for any reason any of the improvements described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(2)(f): (2)(f)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(2)(f)(i): a statement of existing zoning or other planned land use designation of each unit and the proposed use of each unit in the subdivision including uses as residential dwellings, agriculture, churches, schools, low density apartments, high density apartments and hotels, and a subdivision map showing the proposed use, the zoning, or other planned land use designation, unless each unit has the same proposed use, zoning, or other planned land use designation;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(2)(f)(ii): (2)(f)(i) if the subdivision consists of more than one tract or other smaller division, the information and map required by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(2)(g): a map, which need not be drawn to scale, enabling one unfamiliar with the area in which the subdivision is located to reach the subdivision by road or other thoroughfare from a nearby town or city;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(2)(h): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(2)(h)(i): the boundary, course, dimensions, and intended use of the right-of-way and easement grants of record;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(2)(h)(ii): the location of existing underground and utility facilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(2)(h)(iii): any conditions or restrictions governing the location of the facilities within the right-of-way, and easement grants of record, and utility facilities within the subdivision; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(2)(i): any additional information the division may require to assure full and fair disclosure to prospective purchasers.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(3)(a): The public offering statement may not be used for any promotional purposes either before registration of the subdivided lands or before the date the statement becomes effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(3)(b): The statement may be used after it becomes effective only if it is used in its entirety.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(3)(c): A person may not advertise or represent that the division approves or recommends the subdivided lands or their disposition.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(3)(d): No portion of the public offering statement may be underscored, italicized, or printed in larger, heavier, or different color type than the remainder of the statement, unless the division requires it.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(4): 57-11-10
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(4)(a): The division may require the subdivider to alter or amend the proposed public offering statement in order to assure full and fair disclosure to prospective purchasers.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(4)(b): A change in the substance of the promotional plan or plan of disposition or development of the subdivision may not be made after registration without notifying and receiving approval of the division and without making appropriate amendment of the public offering statement.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(4)(c): 57-11-10 A public offering statement is not current unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(4)(c)(i): all amendments are incorporated;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(4)(c)(ii): 57-11-10 the subdivider has timely filed each renewal report required by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(4)(c)(iii): no cease and desist order issued pursuant to this chapter is in effect.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(5): The subdivider must notify the division within five working days if he is convicted of a crime involving fraud, deception, false pretenses, misrepresentation, false advertising, or dishonest dealing in real estate transactions, or has been subject to any injunction or administrative order restraining a false or misleading promotional plan involving land dispositions.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-7(6): The subdivider must notify the division within five working days if the person which owns the subdivided lands files a petition in bankruptcy or if any other event occurs which may have a material adverse effect on the subdivision.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-8 Examination by division on application for registration.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Upon receipt of an application for registration in proper form, the division shall immediately initiate an examination to determine whether:Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-8(1): 57-11-6; 57-11-7 the requirements of Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-8(2): the subdivider has not, or if a corporation or partnership, its officers, directors, general partners, or persons occupying a similar status or performing similar functions, or other principals as defined by the rules of the division have not been convicted of a crime involving land dispositions or any aspect of the land sales business in this state, the United States, or any other state or foreign country within the past 10 years and has not been subject to any injunction or administrative order entered within the past 10 years restraining a false or misleading promotional plan involving land dispositions; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-8(3): the public offering statement requirements of this chapter have been satisfied.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-9 Notice of filing of application for registration -- Division orders of registration or rejection.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-9(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-9(1)(a): Upon receipt of the application for registration in proper form, the division shall issue a notice of filing to the applicant within five business days of the date of receipt of application.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-9(1)(b): Within 30 days from the date of the notice of filing, or, if no notice of filing is issued within the time required, within 35 days from the date of receipt of the application, the division shall register the subdivided lands or reject the registration.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-9(1)(c): If the division has not entered the rejection within 30 days from the date of notice of filing, the land is considered registered unless the applicant has consented in writing to a delay.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-9(2): 57-11-8(1)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-9(2)(a): 57-11-8(1) After inquiry and examination, if the division affirmatively determines that the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-9(2)(b): The division may provide that the public offering statement is not effective until evidence is obtained and made part of the public offering statement that demonstrates that all permits or approvals necessary for the subdivided lands to be put to the use for which they are offered have been granted.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-9(3): 57-11-8(1)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-9(3)(a): 57-11-8(1) After inquiry and examination, if the division determines that any of the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-9(3)(b): If the requirements are not met within the time allowed, the division shall enter an order rejecting the registration, giving the reasons for the rejection.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-9(3)(c): Rejection of the registration is not effective for 20 days, during which time the applicant may request a hearing.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-10 Renewal report -- Renewal fee -- Examination by division -- Annual reports.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-10(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-10(1)(a): Within 30 days after each annual anniversary date of the division's registration of subdivided lands, the subdivider shall file a renewal report in the form the division prescribes together with a renewal fee of $50.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-10(1)(b): The report shall reflect all material changes to information contained in the original application for registration, including any change in ownership of the subdivider.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-10(1)(c): The report shall also indicate the number of units in the subdivision that have been disposed of since the division registered the subdivided lands.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-10(2): 57-11-8; 57-11-8; 57-11-13; Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-10(2)(a): 57-11-8 The division may, upon the filing of a renewal report, initiate a renewal examination of the kind described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-10(2)(b): 57-11-8 If the division determines upon inquiry and examination that the subdivider fails to meet any of the requirements of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-10(2)(c): 57-11-13; Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act If the subdivider does not meet the requirements within the time allowed, the division may, notwithstanding the provisions of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-10(3): The division may permit the filing of annual reports within 30 days after the anniversary date of the consolidated registration in lieu of the anniversary date of the original registration.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11 Rules of division -- Notice and hearing requirements -- Filing advertising material -- Injunctions -- Intervention by division in suits -- General powers of division.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(1): (1)(a); 63G-30-102
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(1)(a): The division shall prescribe reasonable rules which shall be adopted, amended, or repealed only after a public hearing.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(1)(b): (1)(a); 63G-30-102 The division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(1)(b)(i): (1)(a); 63G-30-102 publish notice of the public hearing described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(1)(b)(ii): send a notice to a nonprofit organization which files a written request for notice with the division at least 20 days before the day of the hearing.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(2): The rules shall include but need not be limited to:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(2)(a): provisions for advertising standards to assure full and fair disclosure; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(2)(b): provisions for escrow or trust agreements, performance bonds, or other means reasonably necessary to assure that all improvements referred to in the application for registration and advertising will be completed and that purchasers will receive the interest in land contracted for.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(3): 57-11-6; 57-11-7 These provisions, however, shall not be required if the city or county in which the subdivision is located requires similar means of assurance of a nature and in an amount no less adequate than is required under said rules:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(3)(a): provisions for operating procedures;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(3)(b): 57-11-6; 57-11-7 provisions for a shortened form of registration in cases where the division determines that the purposes of this act do not require a subdivision to be registered pursuant to an application containing all the information required by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(3)(c): other rules necessary and proper to accomplish the purpose of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(4): The division by rule or order, after reasonable notice, may require the filing of advertising material relating to subdivided lands prior to its distribution, provided that the division must approve or reject any advertising material within 15 days from the receipt thereof or the material shall be considered approved.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(5): If it appears that a person has engaged or is about to engage in an act or practice constituting a violation of a provision of this chapter or a rule or order hereunder, the agency, with or without prior administrative proceedings, may bring an action in the district court of the district where said person maintains his residence or a place of business or where said act or practice has occurred or is about to occur, to enjoin the acts or practices and to enforce compliance with this chapter or any rule or order hereunder.  Upon proper showing, injunctive relief or temporary restraining orders shall be granted, and a receiver or conservator may be appointed.  The division shall not be required to post a bond in any court proceedings.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(6): The division shall be allowed to intervene in a suit involving subdivided lands, either as a party or as an amicus curiae, where it appears that the interpretation or constitutionality of any provision of law will be called into question.  In any suit by or against a subdivider involving subdivided lands, the subdivider promptly shall furnish the agency notice of the suit and copies of all pleadings.  Failure to do so may, in the discretion of the division, constitute grounds for the division withholding any approval required by this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(7): The division may:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(7)(a): accept registrations filed in other states or with the federal government;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(7)(b): contract with public agencies or qualified private persons in this state or other jurisdictions to perform investigative functions; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(7)(c): accept grants-in-aid from any source.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-11(8): The division shall cooperate with similar agencies in other jurisdictions to establish uniform filing procedures and forms, uniform public offering statements, advertising standards, rules, and common administrative practices.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-12 Investigatory powers and proceedings of division.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-12(1): The division may:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-12(1)(a): make necessary public or private investigations within or outside of this state to determine whether any person has violated or is about to violate this act or any rule or order hereunder or to aid in the enforcement of this act or in the prescribing of rules and forms hereunder;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-12(1)(b): require or permit any person to file a complaint in the form required by the division as to all the facts and circumstances concerning the matter to be investigated.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-12(2): For the purpose of any investigation or proceeding under this act, the division or any officer designated by rule may administer oaths or affirmations, and upon its own motion or upon request of any party may subpoena witnesses, compel their attendance, take evidence, and require the production of any matter which is relevant to the investigation, including the existence, description, nature, custody, condition and location of any books, documents, or other tangible things and the identity and location of persons having knowledge of relevant facts, or any other matter reasonably calculated to lead to the discovery of material evidence.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-12(3): Upon failure to obey a subpoena or to answer questions propounded by the investigating officer and upon reasonable notice to all persons affected thereby, the division may apply to any district court for an order compelling compliance.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-13 Enforcement powers of division -- Cease and desist orders.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-13(1): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-13(1)(a): If the director has reason to believe that any person has been or is engaging in conduct violating this chapter, or has violated any lawful order or rule of the division, the director shall issue and serve upon the person a cease and desist order and may also order the person to take such affirmative actions the director determines will carry out the purposes of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-13(1)(b): The person served may request an adjudicative proceeding within 10 days after receiving the order.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-13(1)(c): The cease and desist order remains in effect pending the hearing.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-13(1)(d): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act The division shall follow the procedures and requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-13(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-13(2)(a): After the hearing the director may issue an order making the cease and desist order permanent if the director finds there has been a violation of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-13(2)(b): If no hearing is requested and the person served does not obey the director's order, the director shall file suit in the name of the Department of Commerce and the Division of Real Estate to enjoin the person from violating this chapter.  The action shall be filed in the district court in the county in which the conduct occurred or where the person resides or carries on business.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-13(3): The remedies and action provided in this section may not interfere with or prevent the prosecution of any other remedies or actions including criminal prosecutions.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-14 Revocation, suspension, or denial of registration -- Grounds -- Suspension or revocation of license.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-14(1): (1)(b); (1)(a); (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-14(1)(a): (1)(b) If the division makes a written finding of fact that a subdivider engages in one or more acts described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-14(1)(a)(i): deny an application for registration;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-14(1)(a)(ii): revoke, suspend, or deny reissuance of a registration; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-14(1)(a)(iii): impose a civil penalty not to exceed the greater of:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-14(1)(a)(iii)(A): $2,500 for each violation; or
