Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-18 Dispositions subject to chapter -- Jurisdiction of district courts.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Dispositions of subdivided lands are subject to this act, and the district courts of this state have jurisdiction in claims or causes of action arising under this act, if:Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-18(1): The subdivided lands offered for disposition are located in this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-18(2): The subdivider's principal office is located in this state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-18(3): Any offer or disposition of subdivided lands is made in this state, whether or not the offeror or offeree is then present in this state, if the offer originates within this state or is directed by the offeror to a person or place in this state and received by the person or at the place to which it is directed.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-20 Service of process.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-20(1): In addition to the methods of service provided for in the Utah Rules of Civil Procedure, service may be made by delivering a copy of the process to the office of the division, but it is not effective unless the plaintiff, which may be the division in a proceeding instituted by it:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-20(1)(a): forthwith sends a copy of the process and of the pleading by certified or registered mail to the defendant or respondent at his last known address; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-20(1)(b): the plaintiff's affidavit of compliance with this section is filed in the case on or before the return day of the process, if any, or within such further time as the court allows.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-20(2): (1) If any person, including any nonresident of this state, engages in conduct prohibited by this act or any rule or order hereunder, and has not filed a consent to service of process and personal jurisdiction over him cannot otherwise be obtained in this state, that conduct authorizes the division to receive service of process in any noncriminal proceeding against him or his successor which grows out of the conduct and which is brought under this act or any rule or order hereunder, with the same force and validity as if served on him personally. Notice shall be given as provided in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 57-11-21 Uniformity of construction.
----------------------------------------------------------
This act shall be so construed as to effectuate its general purpose to make uniform the law of those states which enact it.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 57 - Chapter 12 - Utah Relocation Assistance Act
****************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-1 Short title.
------------------------------------------
This act shall be known and may be cited as the "Utah Relocation Assistance Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-2 Declaration of policy.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-2(1): It is hereby declared to be the policy of this chapter and of the state, and the Legislature recognizes:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-2(1)(a): that it is often necessary for the various agencies of state and local government to acquire land by condemnation;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-2(1)(b): that persons, businesses, and farms are often uprooted and displaced by such action while being recompensed only for the value of land taken;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-2(1)(c): that such displacement often works economic hardship on those least able to suffer the added and uncompensated costs of moving, locating new homes, business sites, farms, and other costs of being relocated;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-2(1)(d): that such added expenses should reasonably be included as a part of the project cost and paid to those displaced;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-2(1)(e): that the Congress of the United States has established matching grants for relocation assistance, and has also established uniform policies for land acquisition under the Uniform Relocation Assistance and Land Acquisition Policies Act of 1970, 42 U.S.C. 4601 et seq., to assist the states in meeting these expenses and assuring that land is fairly acquired; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-2(1)(f): that it is in the public interest for the state to provide for such payments and to establish such land acquisition policies.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-2(2): Therefore, the purpose of this chapter is to establish a uniform policy for the fair and equitable treatment of persons displaced by the acquisition of real property by state and local land acquisition programs, by building code enforcement activities, or by a program of voluntary rehabilitation of buildings or other improvements conducted pursuant to governmental supervision.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-2(3): All of the provisions of this chapter shall be liberally construed to put into effect the foregoing policies and purposes.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3 Definitions.
------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(1): "Agency" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(1)(a): a department, division, agency, commission, board, council, committee, authority, political subdivision, or other instrumentality of the state or of a political subdivision of the state whether one or more; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(1)(b): any other person whose use of the power of eminent domain results in a person becoming a displaced person.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(2): "Business" means any lawful activity, excepting a farm operation, conducted primarily:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(2)(a): for the purchase, sale, lease, or rental of personal or real property, and for the manufacture, processing, or marketing of products, commodities, or any other personal property;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(2)(b): for the sale of services to the public;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(2)(c): by a nonprofit organization; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(2)(d): for assisting in the purchase, sale, resale, manufacture, processing, or marketing of products, commodities, personal property, or services by the erection and maintenance of an outdoor advertising display or displays, whether or not such display or displays are located on the premises on which any of the above activities are conducted.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(3): 72-1-201 "Department of Transportation" means the Department of Transportation created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(4): "Displaced person" means any person who, after the effective date of this chapter, moves from real property, or who moves the person's personal property from real property, or moves or discontinues the person's business or moves the person's dwelling as a result of the acquisition of the real property, in whole or in part, or as a result of a written order of the acquiring agency to vacate real property for a program of purchase undertaken by an agency or as a direct result of code enforcement activities or a program of rehabilitation of buildings conducted pursuant to a federal or state assisted program.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(5): "Family farm" means a farm operation which is conducted:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(5)(a): on two sections (1280 acres) or less; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(5)(b): as a sole proprietorship or through an entity which is wholly owned by members of the same immediate family.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(6): "Farm operation" means any activity conducted solely or primarily for the production of one or more agricultural products or commodities, including timber, for sale or home use, and customarily producing such products or commodities in sufficient quantity to be capable of contributing materially to the operator's support.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(7): "Nonprofit organization" means all corporations, societies, and associations whose object is not pecuniary profit, but is to promote the general interest and welfare of the members, whether temporal, social, or spiritual.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(8): "Person" means any individual, partnership, corporation, or association.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(9): (9)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(9)(a): "Pole barn" means a building or structure used in conjunction with a farm operation that:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(9)(a)(i): uses poles as the primary load-bearing structure; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(9)(a)(ii): does not have a foundation.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(9)(b): (9)(a) "Pole barn" includes any building or structure that met the definition of a pole barn in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-3(10): "Small business" means a business which has a gross annual income of less than $1,500,000.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-4 Federal funds -- Direct assistance.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-4(1): When federal funds are available for payment of direct financial assistance to a person displaced by acquisition of real property by any agency, the displacing agency may use those federal funds with state or local funds to the extent provided by federal law and may provide direct financial assistance in the instances and on the conditions set forth by federal law and regulations.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-4(2): (3); (2); (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-4(2)(a): When federal funds are not available or used for payment of direct financial assistance to a person displaced by the acquisition of real property by an agency, the displacing agency may provide direct financial assistance to the person.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-4(2)(b): (3); (2); (1) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-4(3): (3)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-4(3)(a): The amount of direct financial assistance provided to a person displaced by acquisition of real property by any agency includes actual reasonable expenses necessary to reestablish a displaced farm, nonprofit organization, or business at a new site, in accordance with criteria established by the agency by rule, but not exceeding $50,000.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-4(3)(b): (3)(a) The $50,000 limit on direct financial assistance established in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-4(3)(b)(i): applies despite any lower limit established by federal statute or regulation or agency rule; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-4(3)(b)(ii): does not apply if a higher limit is established by federal statute or regulation.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-4(4): (4); (4); (4)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-4(4)(a): (4) A displaced person eligible for payments under this chapter who is displaced from the person's place of business or farm may accept payment under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-4(4)(b): (4) A payment under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-4(4)(c): (4) A person whose sole business at the site from which the person is displaced is the rental of property to others does not qualify for payment under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-4(5): Assistance under this section may not be provided to a person who is ineligible to receive relocation assistance under a federal statute or regulation.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-5 Reimbursement of owner for expenses.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Any agency acquiring real property for its use shall as soon as practicable after the date of payment of the purchase price or the date of deposit into court of funds to satisfy the award of compensation in a condemnation proceeding to acquire real property, whichever is the earlier, reimburse the owner for expenses the owner necessarily incurred for:Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-5(1): recording fees, transfer taxes, and similar expenses incidental to conveying the real property to the agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-5(2): penalty costs for prepayment for any preexisting recorded mortgage entered into in good faith encumbering the real property;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-5(3): the pro rata portion of real property taxes paid which are allocable to a period subsequent to the date of vesting title in the agency, or the effective date of possession of such real property by the agency, whichever is the earlier; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-5(4): relocation costs.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-6 Buildings, structures or other improvements.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-6(1): Where any interest in real property is acquired, an equal interest in all buildings, structures, or other improvements located upon the real property so acquired and which is required to be removed from the real property or which is determined to be adversely affected by the use to which the real property will be put, shall be acquired.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-6(2): (1) For the purpose of determining the just compensation to be paid for any building, structure, or other improvement required to be acquired under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-6(3): (2) Payment for the buildings, structures, or improvements as set forth in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-7 Replacement property.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-7(1): No person shall be required to move or be relocated from land used for his residence and acquired under any of the condemnation or eminent domain laws of this state until he has been offered a comparable replacement dwelling, including the curtilage, which is a decent, safe, clean, and sanitary dwelling, including the curtilage, adequate to accommodate the occupants, available on the private market, and reasonably accessible to public services and places of employment.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-7(2): If a program or project cannot proceed to actual construction because comparable sale or rental housing is not available and cannot otherwise be made available, such action shall be taken as is necessary or appropriate to provide this housing by use of funds authorized for the project.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-7(3): No person shall be required to move from his dwelling, including the curtilage, after the effective date of this act because of any project of the agency, unless replacement housing is available to, and offered to the property owner.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-7(4): The agency shall assist owners of small businesses and family farms in identifying replacement properties available on the private market, located within the jurisdiction of the agency.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-8 Advisory program.
-----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-8(1): Whenever the acquisition of real property for a program or project undertaken by an agency will result in the displacement of any person after the effective date of this act, the agency shall provide a relocation assistance advisory program for displaced persons which shall offer the services prescribed in this act. If the agency determines that any person occupying property immediately adjacent to the real property acquired is caused substantial economic injury because of the acquisition, it may offer this person relocation advisory services under such program.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-8(2): (1) Each relocation assistance program required by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-8(2)(a): to determine the needs of displaced persons, business concerns, and nonprofit organizations for relocation assistance;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-8(2)(b): to assist owners of displaced businesses and farm operations in obtaining and becoming established in suitable business locations or replacement farms;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-8(2)(c): to supply information concerning programs of the federal, state, and local governments offering assistance to displaced persons and business concerns;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-8(2)(d): to assist in minimizing hardships to displaced persons in adjusting to relocation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-8(2)(e): to secure, to the greatest extent practicable, the coordination of relocation activities with other project activities and other planned or proposed governmental actions in the community or nearby areas which may affect the carrying out of the relocation program.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-9 Rules of displacing agency.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-9(1): (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-9(1)(a): A displacing agency may enact rules to assure that:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-9(1)(a)(i): the payments and assistance authorized by this chapter are administered in a manner that is fair, reasonable, and as uniform as practicable;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-9(1)(a)(ii): a displaced person who makes proper application for a payment authorized by this chapter is paid promptly after a move or, in hardship cases, is paid in advance; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-9(1)(a)(iii): any person aggrieved by a determination as to eligibility for a payment authorized by this chapter, or the amount of a payment, may have the person's application reviewed by the head of the displacing agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-9(1)(b): (1)(a) Each displacing agency that has not adopted rules under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-9(2): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act Each displacing agency shall comply with the procedures and requirements of

Secs. 4601-4655, for which the Department of Transportation is the displacing agency in a circumstance described in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-9(3)(b): (3)(a) The requirements of Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-9(3)(b)(ii): there is a question of law affecting the denial of a financial assistance claim.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-9(3)(c): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with


Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-10 Displacing agency may contract for services or function through another agency.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
To prevent unnecessary expense and duplication of functions and to promote uniform and effective administration of relocation assistance programs for displaced persons, the displacing agency may enter into contracts with any person for services in connection with these programs, or may carry out its functions under this act through any agency or any federal agency or instrumentality.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-11 Payments not income or resources for welfare or tax purposes.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
No payment received by a displaced person under this act shall be considered as income or resources for the purpose of determining the eligibility or extent of eligibility of any person for assistance under any state law or for the purposes of the state's individual income tax, corporation franchise tax, or other tax laws. These payments shall not be considered as income or resources of any recipient of public assistance, and such payments shall not be deducted from the amount of aid to which the recipient would otherwise be entitled.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-12 Judicial review.
-----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-12(1): Any person aggrieved by an order concerning relocation assistance may obtain judicial review.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-12(2): Venue for judicial review of informal adjudicative proceedings is in the district court of the county in which the real property taken for public use is located.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13 Procedure for acquisition of property.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(1)(a): As used in this section, "fee simple owner" means the owner of a fee simple interest in real property.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(1)(b): "Fee simple owner" does not include a tenant, lienholder, or other claimant of an interest in real property.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(2): (2)(c)(i) Any agency acquiring real property as to which it has the power to acquire under the eminent domain or condemnation laws of this state shall comply with the following policies:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(2)(a): Every reasonable effort shall be made to acquire expeditiously real property by negotiation with the fee simple owner.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(2)(b): Real property shall be appraised before the initiation of negotiations, and the fee simple owner or his designated representative shall be given an opportunity to accompany the appraiser during his inspection of the property.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(2)(c): (2)(c)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(2)(c)(i): Before the initiation of negotiations for real property, an amount shall be established which is reasonably believed to be just compensation therefor, measured by an undivided interest in the real property being acquired, and such amount shall be offered to the fee simple owner for the property.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(2)(c)(ii): (2)(c)(i) In no event shall the amount established as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(2)(c)(iii): Any decrease or increase of the fair market value of real property prior to the date of valuation caused by the public improvement for which such property is acquired or by the likelihood that the property would be acquired for such improvement, other than that due to physical deterioration within the reasonable control of the fee simple owner, will be disregarded in determining the compensation for the property.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(2)(c)(iv): The fee simple owner of the real property to be acquired shall be provided with a written statement of, and summary of the basis for, the amount established as just compensation.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(2)(c)(v): Where appropriate the just compensation for real property acquired and for damages to remaining real property shall be separately stated.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(2)(c)(vi): If a pole barn is impacted as a result of a real property acquisition under this chapter, the acquiring agency shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(2)(c)(vi)(A): determine whether the fee simple owner would receive greater net proceeds by classifying the pole barn as real property or as personal property; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(2)(c)(vi)(B): classify the pole barn in the manner that results in the highest net proceeds to the fee simple owner.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(2)(d): No owner shall be required to surrender possession of real property acquired through federal or federally assisted programs before the agreed purchase price is paid or there is deposited with a court having jurisdiction of condemnation of such property, in accordance with applicable law, for the benefit of the owner an amount not less than the lowest approved appraisal of the fair market value of such property or the amount of the award of compensation in the condemnation proceeding of such property.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(2)(e): The construction or development of a public improvement shall be so scheduled that, to the greatest extent practicable, no person lawfully occupying real property shall be required to move from a dwelling (assuming a replacement dwelling will be available) or to move his business or farm operation without at least 90 days' written notice from the date by which such move is required.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(2)(f): If an owner or tenant is permitted to occupy the real property acquired on a rental basis for a short term or for a period subject to termination on short notice, the amount of rent required shall not exceed the fair rental value of the property to a short-term occupier.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(2)(g): In no event shall the time of condemnation be advanced, on negotiations or condemnation and the deposit of funds in court for the use of the owner be deferred, or any other coercive action be taken to compel an agreement on the price to be paid for the property.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(2)(h): If an interest in real property is to be acquired by exercise of the power of eminent domain, formal condemnation proceedings shall be instituted. The acquiring agency shall not intentionally make it necessary for an owner to institute legal proceedings to prove the fact of the taking of his real property.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-13(2)(i): If the acquisition of only part of the property would leave the fee simple owner with an uneconomic remnant, an offer to acquire the entire property shall be made.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-14 Dispute resolution -- Additional appraisal.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-14(1): 13-43-204 If the agency and the private property owner or displaced person disagree on any issue arising out of this chapter, the private property owner may submit the dispute for mediation or arbitration according to the procedures and requirements of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-14(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-14(2)(a): The private property owner or displaced person may request that the mediator or arbitrator authorize an additional appraisal.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-14(2)(b): If the mediator or arbitrator determines that an additional appraisal is reasonably necessary to reach a resolution of the case, the mediator or arbitrator may:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-14(2)(b)(i): have an additional appraisal of the property prepared by an independent appraiser; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-12-14(2)(b)(ii): require the agency to pay the costs of the first additional appraisal.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 57 - Chapter 13 - Solar Easements
*************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 57-13-1 Definitions.
------------------------------------------
As used in this act:Utah Code Annotated § 57-13-1(1): "Solar easement" means a right, whether or not stated in the form of restriction, easement, covenant, or conditions in any deed, will, or other instrument executed by or on behalf of any owner of land or solar skyspace for the purpose of ensuring adequate exposure of a solar energy system as defined herein.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13-1(2): "Solar energy system" means a system of apparatus and equipment capable of collecting and converting incident solar radiation into heat, or mechanical or electrical energy, and transferring these forms of energy by a separate apparatus to storage or to point of use, including, but not limited to, water heating, space heating or cooling, electric energy generation or mechanical energy generation.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13-1(3): "Passive solar system" means a system which uses structural elements of the building, to provide for collection, storage, and distribution of solar energy for heating or cooling.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13-1(4): "Solar skyspace" means the space between a solar energy collector and the sun which must remain unobstructed such that on any given clear day of the year, not more than 10% of the collectable insolation shall be blocked.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-13-2 Creation of solar easement -- Writing required -- Contents -- Enforcement.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13-2(1): Any property owner may grant a solar easement in the same manner and with the same effect as a conveyance of an interest in real property. The easements shall be created in writing and shall be filed, duly recorded and indexed in the office of the recorder of the county in which the easement is granted. Such easements shall run with the land or lands benefited and burdened and shall constitute a perpetual easement, except that a solar easement may terminate upon the conditions stated herein.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13-2(2): Any deed, will, or other instrument that creates a solar easement shall include, but the contents need not be limited to:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13-2(2)(a): a description of the real property subject to the solar easement and a description of the real property benefiting from the solar easement;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13-2(2)(b): a description of the vertical and horizontal angles, expressed in degrees and measured from the site of the solar energy system, at which the solar easement extends over the real property subject to the solar easement, or any other description which defines the three dimensional space, or the place and times of day in which an obstruction to direct sunlight is prohibited or limited;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13-2(2)(c): any terms or conditions under which the solar easement is granted or may be terminated;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13-2(2)(d): any provisions for compensation of the owner of the real property benefiting from the solar easement in the event of interference with the enjoyment of the solar easement, or compensation of the owner of the real property subject to the solar easement, or compensation of the owner of the real property subject to the solar easement for maintaining the solar easement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13-2(2)(e): any other provisions necessary or desirable to execute the instrument.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13-2(3): A solar easement may be enforced by injunction or proceedings in injunction or other civil action.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 57 - Chapter 13a - Easement for Water Conveyance
****************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 57-13a-101 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 57-13a-101(1): "Water conveyance" means a canal, ditch, pipeline, or other means of conveying water.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13a-101(2): "Water user" means a water user or the water user's predecessor whose water being conveyed is represented by a water right recognized under state law or by shares in a mutual irrigation company.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 57 - Chapter 13b - Easement for Historical Livestock Trail Act
******************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 57-13b-101 Title.
---------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Easement for Historical Livestock Trail Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 57-13b-102 Definition.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter, "historical livestock trail" means property over which livestock has historically traveled to or from a grazing area or market.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-13b-201 Prescriptive easement for livestock trail.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13b-201(1): (1)(a) A prescriptive easement may be established if:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13b-201(1)(a): a property owner uses an historical livestock trail that crosses another person's property for a period of 20 years; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13b-201(1)(b): (1)(a) the use of the other owner's property as an historical livestock trail for the 20-year period described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13b-201(1)(b)(i): continuous;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13b-201(1)(b)(ii): open and notorious; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13b-201(1)(b)(iii): adverse.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13b-201(2): (1)(b)(i); (ii) If a property owner establishes that a use is continuous and open and notorious under Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13b-201(3): (1); (2) Notwithstanding Subsections

******************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(1): "Appurtenant easement" means an easement tied to, or dependent on, ownership or occupancy of a unit or a parcel of real property.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(2): 57-8-3; 57-8a-102; 57-23-2 "Common-interest community" means:

Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(3)(a): retaining or protecting the natural, scenic, wildlife, wildlife-habitat, biological, ecological, or open-space values of real property;

Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(3)(c): protecting natural resources, including wetlands, grasslands, and riparian areas;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(3)(d): maintaining or enhancing air or water quality;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(3)(e): preserving the historical, architectural, archeological, paleontological, or cultural aspects of real property; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(3)(f): Chapter 18, Land Conservation Easement Act any other purpose under
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(4): "Dominant estate" means an estate or interest in real property benefitted by an appurtenant easement.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(5): "Easement" means a nonpossessory property interest that:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(5)(a): provides a right to enter, use, or enjoy real property owned by or in the possession of another; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(5)(b): imposes on the owner or possessor a duty not to interfere with the entry, use, or enjoyment permitted by the instrument creating the easement or, in the case of an easement not established by express grant or reservation, the entry, use, or enjoyment authorized by law.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(6)(b): in the case of an easement in gross, a public-entity easement, a public-utility easement, a conservation easement, or a negative easement, the grantee of the easement or a successor.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(7): "Easement in gross" means an easement not tied to, or dependent on, ownership or occupancy of a unit or a parcel of real property.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(10): "Negative easement" means a nonpossessory property interest whose primary purpose is to impose on a servient estate owner a duty not to engage in a specified use of the estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(11): "Person" means an individual, an estate, a business or a nonprofit entity, a public corporation, a government or governmental subdivision, an agency, or an instrumentality, or other legal entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(12): "Public entity" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(12)(a): the United States;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(12)(b): an agency of the United States;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(12)(c): the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(12)(d): a political subdivision of the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(12)(e): an agency of the state or a political subdivision of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(13): "Public-entity easement" means a nonpossessory property interest in which the easement holder is a public entity.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(15)(a)(ii): a publicly regulated utility or a publicly owned utility under federal law or the laws of this state or a municipality;

Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(17)(b)(ii): Chapter 23, Real Estate Cooperative Marketing Act an interest in a common-interest community, unless the interest is personal property under
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(18): "Record," used as a noun, means information that is inscribed on a tangible medium or that is stored in an electronic or other medium and is retrievable in perceivable form.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(19): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(19)(a): "Security instrument" means a mortgage, a deed of trust, a security deed, a contract for deed, a lease, or other record that creates or provides for an interest in real property to secure payment or performance of an obligation, whether by acquisition or retention of a lien, a lessor's interest under a lease, or title to the real property.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-101(23): "Unit" means a physical portion of a common-interest community designated for separate ownership or occupancy with boundaries described in a declaration establishing the common-interest community.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-103 Right of servient estate owner to relocate easement.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A servient estate owner may relocate an easement under this chapter only if the relocation does not materially:Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-103(1): lessen the utility of the easement;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-103(2): after the relocation, increase the burden on the easement holder in the easement holder's reasonable use and enjoyment of the easement;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-103(3): impair an affirmative, easement-related purpose for which the easement was created;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-103(4): during or after the relocation, impair the safety of the easement holder or another person entitled to use and enjoy the easement;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-103(5): during the relocation, disrupt the use and enjoyment of the easement by the easement holder or another person entitled to use and enjoy the easement, unless the servient estate owner substantially mitigates the duration and nature of the disruption;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-103(6): impair the physical condition, use, or value of the dominant estate or improvements on the dominant estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-103(7): impair the value of the collateral of a security-interest holder of record in the servient estate or dominant estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-103(8): impair a real-property interest of a lessee of record in the dominant estate; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-103(9): impair a recorded real-property interest of any other person in the servient estate or dominant estate.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-109 Limited effect on relocation.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-109(1): Relocation of an easement under this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-109(1)(a): is not a new transfer or a new grant of an interest in the servient estate or the dominant estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-109(1)(b): is not a breach or default of, and does not trigger, a due-on-sale clause or other transfer-restriction clause under a security instrument, except as otherwise determined by a court under a law other than this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-109(1)(c): is not a breach or default of a lease, except as otherwise determined by a court under a law other than this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-109(1)(d): is not a breach or default by the servient estate owner of a recorded document affected by the relocation, except as otherwise determined by a court under a law other than this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-109(1)(e): does not affect the priority of the easement with respect to other recorded real-property interests burdening the area of the servient estate where the easement was located before the relocation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-109(1)(f): is not a fraudulent conveyance or voidable transaction under law.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-109(2): This chapter does not affect any other method of relocating an easement permitted under a law of this state other than this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-110 Nonwaiver.
-------------------------------------------
The right of a servient estate owner to relocate an easement under this chapter may not be waived, excluded, or restricted by agreement even if:Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-110(1): the instrument creating the easement prohibits relocation or contains a waiver, exclusion, or restriction of this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-110(2): the instrument creating the easement requires consent of the easement holder to amend the terms of the easement; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-110(3): the location of the easement is fixed by the instrument creating the easement, another agreement, previous conduct, acquiescence, estoppel, or implication.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-111 Uniformity of application and construction.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
In applying and construing this uniform act, consideration shall be given to the need to promote uniformity of the uniform law with respect to the uniform law's subject matter among the states that enact the uniform law.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-112 Relation to Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
This chapter modifies, limits, or supersedes the Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7001 et seq., but does not modify, limit, or supersede Section 101(c) of that act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7001(c), or authorize electronic delivery of any of the notices described in Section 103(b) of that act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7003(b).

Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-113 Transitional provision.
--------------------------------------------------------
This chapter applies to an easement created before, on, or after May 4, 2022.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-13c-114 Severability.
----------------------------------------------
If any provision of this chapter or the application of the chapter to any person or circumstance is held invalid, the invalidity does not affect other provisions or applications of this chapter that can be given effect without the invalid provision or application, and to this end the provisions of this chapter are severable.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-14-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 57-14-102(1): "Charge" means the admission price or fee asked in return for permission to enter or go upon the land.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-14-102(2): "Child" means an individual who is 16 years old or younger.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-14-102(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-14-102(3)(a): "Land" means any land within the state boundaries.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-14-102(3)(b): "Land" includes roads, railway corridors, water, water courses, private ways and buildings, structures, and machinery or equipment when attached to the realty.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-14-102(4): "Owner" means the possessor of any interest in the land, whether public or private land, including a tenant, a lessor, a lessee, an occupant, or person in control of the land.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-14-102(5): "Person" includes any person, regardless of age, maturity, or experience, who enters upon or uses land for recreational purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-14-102(6): "Recreational purpose" includes, but is not limited to, any of the following or any combination thereof:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-14-102(6)(a): hunting;

Utah Code Annotated - Title 57 - Chapter 16 - Mobile Home Park Residency Act
****************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-1 Short title.
------------------------------------------
This act shall be known and may be cited as the "Mobile Home Park Residency Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-2 Purpose of chapter.
-------------------------------------------------
The fundamental right to own and protect land and to establish conditions for its use by others necessitate that the owner of a mobile home park be provided with speedy and adequate remedies against those who abuse the terms of a tenancy. The high cost of moving mobile homes, the requirements of mobile home parks relating to their installation, and the cost of landscaping and lot preparation necessitate that the owners of mobile homes occupied within mobile home parks be provided with protection from actual or constructive eviction. It is the purpose of this chapter to provide protection for both the owners of mobile homes located in mobile home parks and for the owners of mobile home parks.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3 Definitions.
------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(1): "Amenities" means the following physical, recreational or social facilities located at a mobile home park:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(1)(a): a club house;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(1)(b): a park;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(1)(c): a playground;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(1)(d): a swimming pool;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(1)(e): a hot tub;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(1)(f): a tennis court; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(1)(g): a basketball court.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(2): "Change of use" means a change of the use of a mobile home park, or any part of it, for a purpose other than the rental of mobile home spaces.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(3): "Fees" means other charges incidental to a resident's tenancy including, but not limited to, late fees, charges for pets, charges for storage of recreational vehicles, charges for the use of park facilities, and security deposits.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(4): "Mobile home" means a transportable structure in one or more sections with the plumbing, heating, and electrical systems contained within the unit, which when erected on a site, may be used with or without a permanent foundation as a family dwelling.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(5): "Mobile home park" means any tract of land on which two or more mobile home spaces are leased, or offered for lease or rent, to accommodate mobile homes for residential purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(6): "Mobile home space" means a specific area of land within a mobile home park designed to accommodate one mobile home.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(7): Title 54, Chapter 2, General Provisions; Title 10, Utah Municipal Code "Public utility" means an entity that provides electrical or gas service, including a:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(7)(a): Title 54, Chapter 2, General Provisions public utility as defined in
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(7)(b): Title 10, Utah Municipal Code municipality as defined in
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(8): "Rent" means charges paid for the privilege of occupying a mobile home space, and may include service charges and fees.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(9): "Resident" means an individual who leases or rents space in a mobile home park.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(10): "Service charges" means separate charges paid for the use of electrical and gas service improvements which exist at a mobile home space, or for trash removal, sewage and water, or any combination of the above.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(11): 57-16-4.1(2); 57-16-4.1(3) "Settlement discussion expiration" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(11)(a): 57-16-4.1(2) the resident has failed to give a written notice of dispute within the period specified in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-3(11)(b): 57-16-4.1(3) the resident and management of the mobile home park have met together under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-4 Termination of lease or rental agreement -- Required contents of lease -- Increases in rents or fees -- Required disclosures -- Sale of homes -- Notice regarding planned reduction or restriction of amenities.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-4(1): A mobile home park or its agents may not terminate a lease or rental agreement upon any ground other than as specified in this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-4(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-4(2)(a): A mobile home park and a mobile home park resident that enter into an agreement for the lease of a mobile home park space shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-4(2)(a)(i): enter into the lease agreement in writing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-4(2)(a)(ii): sign the lease agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-4(2)(b): A mobile home park shall, for each lease entered into by the mobile home park with a mobile home park resident:

Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-4(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-4(4)(a): Increases in rent or fees for periodic tenancies are unenforceable until 60 days after notice of the increase is mailed to the resident.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-7(1)(b)(i)(B): 90 days after its promulgation if it is a rule that requires a resident to make exterior, physical improvements to the resident's mobile home or mobile home space and to incur expenses greater than $250 up to $2,000 in order to comply with the rule; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-7(1)(b)(i)(C): 60 days after its promulgation if it is a rule that requires a resident to make exterior, physical improvements to the resident's mobile home or mobile home space and to incur expenses of $250 or less in order to comply with the rule.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-7(2): A mobile home park may specify the type of material used, and the methods used in the installation of, underskirting, awnings, porches, fences, or other additions or alterations to the exterior of a mobile home, and may also specify the tie-down equipment used in a mobile home space, in order to insure the safety and good appearance of the park; but under no circumstances may it require a resident to purchase such material or equipment from a supplier designated by the mobile home park.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-7(3): No mobile home park may charge an entrance fee, exit fee, nor installation fee, but reasonable landscaping and maintenance requirements may be included in the mobile home park rules.  The resident is responsible for all costs incident to connection of the mobile home to existing mobile home park facilities and for the installation and maintenance of the mobile home on the mobile home space.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-7(4): Nothing in this section shall be construed to prohibit a mobile home park from requiring a reasonable initial security deposit.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-8 Payment of rent and fees during pendency of eviction proceeding.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If a resident elects to contest an eviction proceeding, all rents, fees, and service charges due and incurred during the pendency of the action shall be paid into court according to the current mobile home park payment schedule. Failure of the resident to pay such amounts may, in the discretion of the court, constitute grounds for granting summary judgment in favor of the mobile home park.  Upon final termination of the issues between the parties, the court shall order all amounts paid into court paid to the mobile home park. The prevailing party is also entitled to court costs and reasonable attorney's fees.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-10 Utility service to mobile home parks -- Limitation on providers' charges.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Local water, sewer, and sanitation entities, including those administered by municipalities and counties which provide water, sewer, or garbage collection services shall not receive a greater percentage net return from supplying a mobile home park than said entity receives from other residential customers. The net return is determined by taking into consideration the costs of maintenance and depreciation of the mobile home park facilities and all savings on administrative costs, including cost of billing residents.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-11 Rights and remedies not exclusive.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
The rights and remedies granted by this chapter are cumulative and not exclusive.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-12 Waiver of rights and duties prohibited.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
No park or resident may agree to waive any right, duty, or privilege conferred by this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-13 Abandonment.
-------------------------------------------
Abandonment of a mobile home space and a mobile home within a mobile home park is presumed in either of the following situations:Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-13(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-13(1)(a): the resident or occupant of the mobile home has not notified the park that the resident or occupant will be absent from the mobile home space or mobile home, and the resident or occupant fails to pay rent within 45 days after the due date; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-13(1)(b): the mobile home park owner has no reasonable evidence, other than the presence of the resident's or occupant's personal property, that the resident or occupant is continuing to occupy the mobile home space and the mobile home; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-13(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-13(2)(a): the resident or occupant of the mobile home has not notified the park that the resident or occupant will be absent from the mobile home space where the mobile home is located, and the resident or occupant fails to pay rent when due; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-13(2)(b): the resident's or occupant's personal property has been removed from the mobile home, and there is no reasonable evidence that the resident or occupant is occupying the mobile home space or mobile home.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16 Mobile home park residents' associations.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(1)(a): "Park operator" means an owner, operator, or manager of a mobile home park, including an employee, agent, or independent contractor of the owner, operator, or manager.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(1)(b): "Primary resident association" means, for a mobile home park with more than one resident association, the resident association that has more members than any other resident association within the mobile home park.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(1)(c): "Resident association" means an organization of mobile home park residents organized to address their common interests and concerns related to the mobile home park.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(1)(d): "Resident entity" means a noncommercial entity that:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(1)(d)(i): advocates for residents of the mobile home park; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(1)(d)(ii): addresses issues relating to mobile home parks that affect or are of concern to residents of the mobile home park.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(2)(a): Residents in a mobile home park may:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(2)(a)(i): form a resident association; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(2)(a)(ii): participate in a regional, state, or national resident association or advocacy group.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(2)(b): A resident association may limit membership in a resident association to owners of manufactured homes within a mobile home park if the purpose of the resident association is to purchase some or all of the mobile home park.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(2)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(2)(c)(i): There may be more than one resident association for a mobile home park.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(2)(c)(ii): A park operator is not required to acknowledge any resident association other than the primary resident association.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(3): At a meeting at which a majority of members are present, resident association members may:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(3)(a): elect officers of the resident association; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(3)(b): adopt bylaws of the resident association.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(4)(a): Except in an emergency, a resident association shall provide seven days' notice of a resident association meeting to all residents of the mobile home park.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(4)(b): A resident of a mobile home park may attend a meeting of a resident association, whether or not the resident is a member of the resident association.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(5): (5)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(5)(a): An officer or member of a resident association may not be held personally responsible or liable for an act or omission of the resident association or of another officer or member of the resident association.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(5)(b): (5)(a) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(6): A park operator may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(6)(a): be a member of a resident association;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(6)(b): attend a meeting of the resident association unless given a written invitation to the meeting by an officer of the resident association;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(6)(c): unlawfully interfere with the resident association's operation;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(6)(d): interfere with a resident's right to contact a state or local health department, a municipality, or other group to complain about the health and safety conditions of the mobile home park; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(6)(e): harass or threaten a resident association.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(7): A resident association may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(7)(a): impose fees, dues, or assessments, upon its members unless a majority of the members agree to the imposition of fees, dues, or assessments; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(7)(b): harass or threaten a park operator.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(8): A park operator shall permit meetings by a resident association located within the park relating to manufactured home living or social or educational purposes, including forums for or speeches by public officials or candidates for public office.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(9): Except for reasonable time, place, and manner limitations, a park operator may not prohibit or adopt a rule prohibiting a mobile home park resident or a resident entity from exercising within the mobile home park the right of free expression for noncommercial purposes, including peacefully organizing, assembling, canvassing, petitioning, leafleting, or distributing written, noncommercial material within the mobile home park.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(10): (10)(e)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(10)(a): A resident association may schedule with the park operator the use of the mobile home park's common facilities, if any, free of charge.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(10)(b): A resident association is responsible for any damage to the mobile home park's common facilities caused by a member of the resident association or a guest or invitee while the resident association uses a common facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(10)(c): A park operator may reasonably limit the frequency of a resident association's use of a common facility if the limitation allows use at least once per week.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(10)(d): (10)(e) A park operator may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(10)(d)(i): charge a resident or resident association a security deposit to use a common facility of the mobile home park that exceeds the amount normally and uniformly charged as a security deposit for use of the common facility; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(10)(d)(ii): (10)(e) except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(10)(e): A park operator may require liability insurance if:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(10)(e)(i): the rules of the mobile home park permit the consumption of alcoholic beverages in a common facility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(10)(e)(ii): alcoholic beverages are to be served at a meeting or private function of the resident association in the common facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(11): (11)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(11)(a): A park operator may not alter or refuse to renew an existing rental agreement, change a rule of the mobile home park, enforce a mobile home park rule in an unreasonable or nonuniform way, bring or threaten to bring an eviction action or other civil action, or take any other action in retaliation based primarily on a resident:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(11)(a)(i): expressing an intention to complain or having complained to a governmental agency about a matter relating to the mobile home park;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(11)(a)(ii): making a complaint in good faith to the park operator;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(11)(a)(iii): filing or expressing an intention to file a lawsuit or administrative action against the park operator; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(11)(a)(iv): testifying in a judicial or administrative proceeding or before a public body.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(11)(b): (11)(a) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(12): This section may not be construed to prohibit a park operator from:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(12)(a): evicting a tenant as provided in other provisions of this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-16(12)(b): exercising other rights the park operator has under applicable law.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-17 Authority of political subdivisions.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
This chapter does not prevent a city, county, or municipality from mediating and enforcing state statutes governing a mobile home park.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-18 Notice required for change in land use or condemnation -- Local ordinances forbidden.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-18(1): (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-18(1)(a): The owner of a mobile home park shall send notice using first-class mail to each resident of the mobile home park of any planned change in land use or condemnation of the park or any portion of the park at least nine months before the day on which the resident is required to vacate the mobile home park.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-18(1)(b): (1)(a) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-18(2): (1) If the planned change in land use or condemnation requires the approval of a governmental agency, the mobile home park owner, in addition to the notice required by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-18(3): (1) If a resident is not a resident of the mobile home park at the time notice was sent under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-18(4): (1) During the period of time between the provision of notice under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-16-18(5): A town, city, or county may not enact any ordinance governing the closure of a mobile home park.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated - Title 57 - Chapter 17 - Residential Renters' Deposits
***************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 57-17-1 Return or explanation of retainage upon termination of tenancy.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Owners or designated agents requiring deposits however denominated from renters leasing or renting residential dwelling units shall either return those deposits at the termination of the tenancy or provide the renter with written notice explaining why any deposit refundable under the terms of the lease or rental agreement is being retained.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-17-2 Non-refundable deposit -- Written notice required.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If there is a written agreement and if any part of the deposit is to be made non-refundable, it must be so stated in writing to the renter at the time the deposit is taken by the owner or designated agent.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-17-3 Deductions from deposit -- Written itemization -- Time for return.

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The holder of the owner's or designated agent's interest in the premises at the time of termination of the tenancy shall be bound by the provisions of this act.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 57 - Chapter 18 - Land Conservation Easement Act
****************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-1 Short title.
------------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Land Conservation Easement Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-2 Definition and characteristics of conservation easement.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-2(1): As used in this chapter, "conservation easement" means an easement, covenant, restriction, or condition in a deed, will, or other instrument signed by or on behalf of the record owner of the underlying real property for the purpose of preserving and maintaining land or water areas predominantly in a natural, scenic, or open condition, or for recreational, agricultural, cultural, wildlife habitat or other use or condition consistent with the protection of open land.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-2(2): A conservation easement is an interest in land and runs with the land benefited or burdened by the easement.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-2(3): A conservation easement is valid whether it is appurtenant or in gross.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-2(4): A conservation easement is enforceable by the holder to the easement and its successors and assigns.  A conservation easement is enforceable against the grantor and its successors and assigns.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-3 Acquisition of conservation easement.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
A charitable organization which qualifies as being tax exempt under Section 501(c)(3) of the Internal Revenue Code or a governmental entity may acquire a conservation easement by purchase, gift, devise, grant, lease, or bequest.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-4 Requirements for creation.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-4(1): 57-18-3 Any property owner may grant a conservation easement to any other qualified person as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-4(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-4(2)(a): A conservation easement shall be in writing and shall be recorded in the office of the recorder of the county in which the easement is granted.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-4(2)(b): Within 10 days after a conservation easement is recorded, the owner of real property for which the conservation easement is granted shall deliver to the assessor of the county in which the property is located a copy of the conservation easement and proof that the conservation easement has been recorded.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-4(2)(c): Before January 1, 2012, each owner of property subject to a conservation easement recorded before May 10, 2011, shall deliver to the assessor of the county in which the property is located a copy of the conservation easement and proof that the conservation easement has been recorded.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-4(3): The instrument that creates a conservation easement shall identify and describe the land subject to the conservation easement by legal description, specify the purpose for which the easement is created, and include a termination date or a statement that the easement continue in perpetuity.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-4(4): 57-18-3 Any qualified person, as defined in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-5 Termination.
------------------------------------------
A conservation easement may be terminated, in whole or in part, by release, abandonment, merger, nonrenewal, conditions set forth in the instrument creating the conservation easement, or in any other lawful manner in which easements may be terminated.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-6 Enforcement.
------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-6(1): A conservation easement may be enforced or protected by injunctive relief granted by a court in a proceeding initiated by the grantor or holder of the easement.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-6(2): In addition to injunctive relief, the holder of a conservation easement is entitled to recover money damages.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-6(3): The holder of a conservation easement may enter the real property burdened or benefited by the easement at reasonable times and in a reasonable manner to ensure compliance.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-7 Conservation easement not obtained through eminent domain -- Conservation easement may not interfere with eminent domain.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-7(1): No conservation easement, or right-of-way or access to a conservation easement may be obtained through the use of eminent domain.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-18-7(2): Title 78B, Chapter 6, Part 5, Eminent Domain The existence of a conservation easement may not defeat or interfere with the otherwise proper exercise of eminent domain under


Utah Code Annotated - Title 57 - Chapter 19 - Timeshare and Camp Resort Act
***************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-1 Short title.
------------------------------------------
This chapter is known and may be cited as the "Timeshare and Camp Resort Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2 Definitions.
------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(1): "Accommodation" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(1)(a): a hotel or motel room;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(1)(b): a condominium or cooperative unit;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(1)(c): a cabin;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(1)(d): a lodge;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(1)(e): an apartment; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(1)(f): a private or commercial structure designed for overnight occupancy by one or more individuals.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(2): "Advertisement" means a written, printed, oral, audio, electronic, or visual offer that:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(2)(a): is made by direct or general solicitation to one or more individuals; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(2)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(2)(b)(i): contains an offer to sell an interest; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(2)(b)(ii): contains a solicitation to visit or obtain additional information about a development.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(3): 57-19-9 "Amendment" means a change to an approved registration that is required under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(4): "Association" means an organized body consisting solely of owners of timeshare interests in a timeshare development, including developers or purchasers.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(5): "Business day" means a day other than a Saturday, Sunday, or state or federal holiday.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(6): "Camping site" means a space designed or promoted for the purpose of locating a trailer, tent, tent trailer, recreational vehicle, pickup camper, motor home, or other similar device used for land-based portable housing.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(7): "Camp resort" means an enterprise that has as its primary purpose the offering of a camp resort interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(8): "Camp resort interest" means the right to use and occupy a camping site.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(9): "Consolidation" means the registration of one or more additional sites or interests in a development after the division approves the development's registration.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(10): "Developer" means a person that:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(10)(a): establishes, owns, offers, sells, or operates a timeshare development or camp resort; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(10)(b): engages one or more other persons to establish, own, offer, sell, or operate a timeshare development or camp resort on the person's behalf.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(11): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(11)(a): "Development" means an enterprise with the primary purpose of offering an interest in a camp resort or timeshare development.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(11)(b): "Development" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(11)(b)(i): a single-site development; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(11)(b)(ii): a multiple-site development.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(12): "Director" means the director of the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(13): "Direct sales presentation" means an in-person, telephonic, or Internet-based communication that presents an offer to purchase an interest in a development to one or more prospective purchasers.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(14): "Division" means the Division of Real Estate of the Department of Commerce.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(15): "Executive director" means the executive director of the Department of Commerce.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(16): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(16)(a): "Interest" means a right that a purchaser receives in exchange for consideration to use and occupy a camping site or an accommodation in a development:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(16)(a)(i): on a recurring basis; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(16)(a)(ii): for a period of time that is less than one year during any given year, regardless of whether the time is determined in advance.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(16)(b): "Interest" includes a membership agreement, sale, lease, deed, license, or right-to-use agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(17): "Offer" means a solicitation solely intended to result in a person purchasing an interest in a development.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(18): 57-19-11 "Property report" means the form of a written disclosure described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(19): "Purchaser" means a person who purchases an interest in a development.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(20): 57-19-5; 57-19-15 "Registration" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(20)(a): 57-19-5 for a development, an approved application for registration described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(20)(b): 57-19-15 for a salesperson, an approved application for registration described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(21): "Renewal" or "renew" means extending a development's or a salesperson's registration for an additional period on or before the registration's expiration date.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(22): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(22)(a): "Sale" or "sell" means selling an interest in a development for value.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(22)(b): "Sale" or "sell" does not include charging a reasonable fee to offset the administrative costs of transferring an interest in a development.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(23): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(23)(a): "Salesperson" means an individual who, for compensation and as agent for another, is engaged in obtaining commitments of persons to purchase an interest in a development by making direct sales presentations to those persons.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(23)(b): "Salesperson" does not include a purchaser or an owner of a timeshare interest engaged in the referral of persons without making a direct sales presentation.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(24): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(24)(a): "Site" means a geographic location where one or more camping sites or accommodations are located.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(24)(b): "Site" includes a geographic location where one or more camping sites or accommodations are located that is constructed in phases and is under common management.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(25): "Timeshare development" means an enterprise with the primary purpose of offering a timeshare interest, including an interest that gives the purchaser the right to use and occupy an accommodation at a single- or multiple-site development.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(26): "Timeshare estate" means a small, undivided fractional fee interest in real property by which the purchaser does not receive any right to use an accommodation except as provided by contract, declaration, or other instrument defining a legal right.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(27): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(27)(a): "Timeshare interest" means a right to occupy fixed or variable accommodations during three or more separate fixed or variable time periods over a period of at least three years, including renewal options, whether or not coupled with an estate in land.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-2(27)(b): "Timeshare interest" includes a timeshare estate.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-3 Rules.
------------------------------------
The director may make, amend, and repeal rules, forms, and orders when necessary to carry out the provisions of this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-4 Unregistered sales prohibited.
------------------------------------------------------------
Except as provided in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-7 Prior permits.
--------------------------------------------
Any permit to market a development issued by the division before April 27, 1987, is considered to be an effective registration, but is subject to the renewal provisions of this chapter upon the anniversary date of the issuance of the original permit.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-10 Effect of application or registration -- Misleading statements to prospective purchasers a misdemeanor.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-10(1): Neither the fact that an application for registration or the written disclosures required by this chapter have been filed, nor the fact that a development has been effectively registered or exempted, constitutes a finding by the director that the offering or any document filed under this chapter is true, complete, and not misleading, nor does either of these facts mean that the director has determined in any way the merits or qualifications of, or recommended or given approval to, any person, developer, or transaction involving an interest in a development.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-10(2): It is a class A misdemeanor to make or cause to be made to any purchaser or prospective purchaser any offering or document filed under this chapter that is untrue, incomplete, or misleading.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-11 Disclosure required.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-11(1): 57-19-26 Except as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-11(2): (1) The written disclosure described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-11(2)(a): may include electronic files; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-11(2)(b): shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-11(2)(b)(i): be on the property report form required by the division; and

Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-11(2)(b)(ii)(A): the name and address of the developer;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-11(2)(b)(ii)(B): a statement regarding whether the developer has ever been convicted of a felony or any misdemeanor involving theft, fraud, or dishonesty, or enjoined from, assessed any civil penalty for, or found to have engaged in the violation of any law designed to protect consumers;
