Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-11(2)(b)(ii)(F): a statement that the development will not issue more interests during a 12-month period than the development can accommodate during the 12-month period;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-11(2)(b)(ii)(G): any event that has occurred since the date of the offer that may have a material adverse effect on the operation of the development; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-11(2)(b)(ii)(H): any other information the director considers necessary for the protection of purchasers.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-12 Purchaser's right to cancel.
-----------------------------------------------------------
"PURCHASER'S RIGHT TO CANCEL: YOU MAY CANCEL THIS AGREEMENT WITHOUT ANY CANCELLATION FEE OR OTHER PENALTY BY HAND DELIVERING OR SENDING BY CERTIFIED MAIL, RETURN RECEIPT REQUESTED, OR A DELIVERY SERVICE THAT PROVIDES PROOF OF DELIVERY, WRITTEN NOTICE OF CANCELLATION TO:  (NAME AND ADDRESS OF DEVELOPER).  THE NOTICE MUST BE DELIVERED OR POSTMARKED BY MIDNIGHT OF THE FIFTH BUSINESS DAY FOLLOWING THE DAY ON WHICH THE AGREEMENT IS SIGNED.  IN COMPUTING THE NUMBER OF BUSINESS DAYS, THE DAY ON WHICH THE CONTRACT IS SIGNED IS NOT INCLUDED."Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-12(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-12(1)(a): An agreement to purchase an interest in a development may be cancelled, at the option of the purchaser, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-12(1)(a)(i): the purchaser delivers a written notice of cancellation to the developer at the developer's business address by:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-12(1)(a)(i)(A): hand; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-12(1)(a)(i)(B): certified mail, return receipt requested, or a delivery service that provides proof of delivery; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-12(1)(a)(ii): the notice is delivered or postmarked not later than midnight of the fifth business day after the day on which the agreement is signed.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-12(1)(b): In computing the number of business days for purposes of this section, the day on which the agreement was signed is not included.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-12(1)(c): Within 30 days after the day on which the developer receives a timely notice of cancellation, the developer shall refund any money or other consideration paid by the purchaser.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-12(2): Every agreement to purchase an interest in a development that is subject to this chapter shall include the following statement in at least 10-point bold upper-case type, immediately preceding the space for the purchaser's signature:

Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-17 Administrative procedures.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-17(1): 57-19-13; 57-19-16 The director may summarily deny an application for registration under any of the provisions of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-17(2): Title 13, Chapter 1, Department of Commerce Before an existing registration is suspended or revoked, or a fine imposed, the director shall schedule a hearing before an administrative law judge and give notice in writing to the affected person as prescribed in
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-17(3): The developer or salesperson has the right to appear at the hearing, in person or by counsel, to be heard and to examine witnesses appearing in connection with the complaint.  At the hearing, all witnesses shall be sworn by the administrative law judge, and stenographic notes or a tape recording of the proceeding shall be taken and filed as a part of the record in the case.  Any party to the proceeding shall be furnished a copy of the stenographic notes or tape recording at a reasonable cost.  The administrative law judge shall render a decision within 60 days after the completion of the hearing.  The executive director and the director shall concurrently make the final decision and promptly notify the parties to the proceedings, in writing, of the ruling, order, or decision.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-17(4): The developer or salesperson, or any person aggrieved, may appeal any adverse ruling, order, or decision of the executive director and the director to the district court for the county in which the hearing was held, within 30 days from the date of service of notice of the ruling, order, or decision upon him.  At the time of filing the notice of appeal, the appellant shall file with the notice a bond for costs on appeal in the amount of $200, conditioned to secure the payment of costs if the appeal is dismissed or the judgment affirmed.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-18 Investigation -- Publication.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-18(1): The director may make any investigations or requests for information, within or outside of this state, that he considers necessary:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-18(1)(a): to determine whether any registration under this chapter should be granted, denied, or revoked;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-18(1)(b): to determine whether any person has violated or is about to violate any of the provisions of this chapter or any rule or order under this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-18(1)(c): to aid in the enforcement of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-18(2): The director may publish information concerning any violation of this chapter or any rule or order under this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-19 Subpoenas -- Evidence.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-19(1): For the purposes of any investigation or proceeding under this chapter, the director, or any officer designated by him, may administer oaths and affirmations, subpoena witnesses, compel their attendance, take evidence, and require the production of any books, papers, correspondence, memoranda, agreements, or other documents or records which the director considers relevant or material to the inquiry.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-19(2): 78B-6-313 A person who disobeys any subpoena lawfully issued by the director, or who refuses to testify to any matters regarding which he may be lawfully interrogated, is subject to the provisions of Section


Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-20 Injunctive relief -- Cease and desist order.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-20(1): Whenever it appears to the director that any person has engaged or is about to engage in any act or practice constituting a violation of any provision of this chapter, and that it would be in the public interest to stop those acts or practices, the director may either:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-20(1)(a): seek injunctive relief as provided in Rule 65A, Utah Rules of Civil Procedure; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-20(1)(b): issue an administrative cease and desist order.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-20(2): (1); Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act If an administrative cease and desist order is issued pursuant to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-20(3): If, at the hearing, a finding is made that there has been a violation of this chapter, the director, with the concurrence of the executive director, may issue an order making the cease and desist order permanent.  If no hearing is requested, and if the person fails to cease the act or practice, or after discontinuing the act or practice again commences it, the director shall file suit in the district court of the county in which the act or practice occurred, or where the person resides or carries on business, to enjoin and restrain the person from violating this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-20(4): Whether or not the director has issued a cease and desist order, the attorney general, in the name of the state or of the director, may bring an action in any court of competent jurisdiction to enjoin any act or practice constituting a violation of any provision of this chapter, and to enforce compliance with this chapter or any rule or order under this chapter.  Upon a proper showing, a permanent or temporary injunction, restraining order, or writ of mandamus shall be granted.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-20(1): Whenever it appears to the director that any person has engaged or is about to engage in any act or practice constituting a violation of any provision of this chapter, and that it would be in the public interest to stop those acts or practices, the director may either:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-20(1)(a): seek injunctive relief as provided in Rule 65A, Utah Rules of Civil Procedure; or

Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-20(3): Title 78A, Judiciary and Judicial Administration

Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-20(3)(b): Title 78A, Judiciary and Judicial Administration If no hearing is requested, and if the person fails to cease the act or practice, or after discontinuing the act or practice again commences the act or practice, the director shall bring an action in a court with jurisdiction under

Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-21 Voidable agreements.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-21(1): 57-19-4; 57-19-14 Any agreement to purchase an interest in a development that violates Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-21(2): No suit under this section may be brought more than two years after the later of:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-21(2)(a): the day on which the agreement is signed; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-21(2)(b): the day on which the purchaser knew or reasonably should have known of the violation.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-22 Violation a misdemeanor.
-------------------------------------------------------
Any person who willfully violates any provision of this chapter is guilty of a class B misdemeanor.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-23 Prosecution.
-------------------------------------------
The director may refer any available evidence concerning violations of this chapter or of any rule or order under this chapter to the attorney general or the proper prosecuting attorney, who may, in his discretion, with or without such a referral, institute the appropriate civil or criminal proceedings under this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-24 Violation of Consumer Sales Practice Act.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
For purposes of applying

Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-25 Remedies nonexclusive.
-----------------------------------------------------
The remedies provided in this chapter are cumulative and nonexclusive, and do not affect any other remedy available at law.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-26 Exemptions.
------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-19-26(1): 57-19-11; 57-19-12 Unless entered into for the purpose of evading the provisions of this chapter, the following transactions are exempt from registration:

Utah Code Annotated - Title 57 - Chapter 20 - Local Rent Control Prohibition
****************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 57-20-1 Rent and fee control prohibition.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-20-1(1): A county, city, or town may not enact an ordinance or resolution that would control rents or fees on private residential property unless it has the express approval of the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-20-1(2): This section does not impair the right of a state agency, county, city, or town to enforce its zoning, building, and planning authority.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 57 - Chapter 21 - Utah Fair Housing Act
*******************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-1 Short title.
------------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Utah Fair Housing Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2 Definitions.
------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(1): 16-6a-102 "Affiliate" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(2): "Aggrieved person" includes a person who:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(2)(a): claims to have been injured by a discriminatory housing practice; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(2)(b): believes that the person will be injured by a discriminatory housing practice that is about to occur.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(3): "Commission" means the Labor Commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(4): "Complainant" means an aggrieved person, including the director, who has commenced a complaint with the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(5): "Conciliation" means the attempted resolution of an issue raised in a complaint of discriminatory housing practices by the investigation of the complaint through informal negotiations involving the complainant, the respondent, and the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(6): "Conciliation agreement" means a written agreement setting forth the resolution of the issues in conciliation.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(7): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act "Conciliation conference" means the attempted resolution of an issue raised in a complaint or by the investigation of a complaint through informal negotiations involving the complainant, the respondent, and the division.  The conciliation conference is not subject to
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(8): "Covered multifamily dwelling" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(8)(a): a building consisting of four or more dwelling units if the building has one or more elevators; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(8)(b): the ground floor units in other buildings consisting of four or more dwelling units.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(9): "Director" means the director of the division or a designee.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(10): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(10)(a): "Disability" means a physical or mental impairment that substantially limits one or more of a person's major life activities, including a person having a record of such an impairment or being regarded as having such an impairment.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(10)(b): "Disability" does not include current illegal use of, or addiction to, any federally controlled substance, as defined in Section 102 of the Controlled Substances Act, 21 U.S.C. Sec. 802.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(11): "Discriminate" includes segregate or separate.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(12): "Discriminatory housing practice" means an act that is unlawful under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(13): "Division" means the Division of Antidiscrimination and Labor established under the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(14): (14)(a) "Dwelling" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(14)(a): a building or structure, or a portion of a building or structure, occupied as, designed as, or intended for occupancy as a residence of one or more families; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(14)(b): (14)(a) vacant land that is offered for sale or lease for the construction or location of a dwelling as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(15): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(15)(a): "Familial status" means one or more individuals who have not attained the age of 18 years being domiciled with:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(15)(a)(i): a parent or another person having legal custody of the one or more individuals; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(15)(a)(ii): the designee of the parent or other person having custody, with the written permission of the parent or other person.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(15)(b): The protections afforded against discrimination on the basis of familial status apply to a person who:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(15)(b)(i): is pregnant;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(15)(b)(ii): is in the process of securing legal custody of any individual who has not attained the age of 18 years; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(15)(b)(iii): is a single individual.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(16): "Gender identity" has the meaning provided in the Diagnostic and Statistical Manual (DSM-5).  A person's gender identity can be shown by providing evidence, including, but not limited to, medical history, care or treatment of the gender identity, consistent and uniform assertion of the gender identity, or other evidence that the gender identity is sincerely held, part of a person's core identity, and not being asserted for an improper purpose.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(17): "National origin" means the place of birth of an individual or of any lineal ancestors.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(18): "Person" includes one or more individuals, corporations, limited liability companies, partnerships, associations, labor organizations, legal representatives, mutual companies, joint-stock companies, trusts, unincorporated organizations, trustees, trustees in cases under the United States Bankruptcy Code, receivers, and fiduciaries.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(19): 63G-4-103 "Presiding officer" has the same meaning as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(20): 61-2f-102 "Real estate broker" or "salesperson" means a principal broker, an associate broker, or a sales agent as those terms are defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(21): "Respondent" means a person against whom a complaint of housing discrimination has been initiated.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(22): "Sex" means gender and includes pregnancy, childbirth, and disabilities related to pregnancy or childbirth.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(23): "Sexual orientation" means an individual's actual or perceived orientation as heterosexual, homosexual, or bisexual.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2(24): "Source of income" means the verifiable condition of being a recipient of federal, state, or local assistance, including medical assistance, or of being a tenant receiving federal, state, or local subsidies, including rental assistance or rent supplements.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2.5 Supremacy over local regulations -- No special class created for other purposes.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2.5(1): This chapter supersedes and preempts any ordinance, regulation, standard, or other legal action by a local government entity, a state entity, or the governing body of a political subdivision that relates to the prohibition of discrimination in housing.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2.5(2): This chapter shall not be construed to create a special or protected class for any purpose other than housing.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-2.7 Nonseverability.
------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-4 Conduct and requirements excluded -- Defenses.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-4(1): 57-21-5(4) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-4(1)(a): require any person to exercise a higher degree of care toward a person who has a disability than toward a person who does not have a disability;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-4(1)(b): relieve any person of obligations generally imposed on all persons regardless of disability in a written lease, rental agreement, contract of purchase or sale, mortgage, trust deed, or other financing agreement; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-4(1)(c): prohibit any program, service, facility, or privilege intended to habilitate, rehabilitate, or accommodate a person with a disability.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-4(2): It is a defense to a complaint or action brought under this chapter that the complainant has a disability that, in the circumstances and even with reasonable accommodation, poses a serious threat to the health or safety of the complainant or others.  The burden of proving this defense is upon the respondent.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5 Discriminatory practices enumerated -- Protected persons, classes enumerated.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(1): It is a discriminatory housing practice to do any of the following because of a person's race, color, religion, sex, national origin, familial status, source of income, disability, sexual orientation, or gender identity:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(1)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(1)(a)(i): refuse to sell or rent after the making of a bona fide offer;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(1)(a)(ii): refuse to negotiate for the sale or rental; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(1)(a)(iii): otherwise deny or make unavailable a dwelling from any person;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(1)(b): discriminate against a person in the terms, conditions, or privileges:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(1)(b)(i): of the sale or rental of a dwelling; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(1)(b)(ii): in providing facilities or services in connection with the dwelling; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(1)(c): represent to a person that a dwelling is not available for inspection, sale, or rental when the dwelling is available.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(2): It is a discriminatory housing practice to make a representation orally or in writing or make, print, circulate, publish, post, or cause to be made, printed, circulated, published, or posted any notice, statement, or advertisement, or to use any application form for the sale or rental of a dwelling, that directly or indirectly expresses any preference, limitation, or discrimination based on race, color, religion, sex, national origin, familial status, source of income, disability, sexual orientation, or gender identity, or expresses any intent to make any such preference, limitation, or discrimination.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(3): It is a discriminatory housing practice to induce or attempt to induce, for profit, a person to buy, sell, or rent a dwelling by making a representation about the entry or prospective entry into the neighborhood of persons of a particular race, color, religion, sex, national origin, familial status, source of income, disability, sexual orientation, or gender identity.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(4): A discriminatory housing practice includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(4)(a): a refusal to permit, at the expense of the person with a disability, reasonable modifications of existing premises occupied or to be occupied by the person if the modifications are necessary to afford that person full enjoyment of the premises, except that in the case of a rental, the landlord, where it is reasonable to do so, may condition permission for a modification on the renter agreeing to restore the interior of the premises, when reasonable, to the condition that existed before the modification, reasonable wear and tear excepted;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(4)(b): a refusal to make a reasonable accommodation in a rule, policy, practice, or service when the accommodation may be necessary to afford the person equal opportunity to use and enjoy a dwelling; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(4)(c): in connection with the design and construction of covered multifamily dwellings for first occupancy after March 13, 1991, a failure to design and construct the covered multifamily dwellings in a manner that:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(4)(c)(i): the covered multifamily dwellings have at least one building entrance on an accessible route, unless it is impracticable to have one because of the terrain or unusual characteristics of the site; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(4)(c)(ii): with respect to covered multifamily dwellings with a building entrance on an accessible route:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(4)(c)(ii)(A): the public use and common use portions of the covered multifamily dwelling are readily accessible to and usable by a person with a disability;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(4)(c)(ii)(B): all the doors designed to allow passage into and within the covered multifamily dwellings are sufficiently wide to allow passage by a person with a disability who is in a wheelchair; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(4)(c)(ii)(C): all premises within the covered multifamily dwellings contain the following features of adaptive design:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(4)(c)(ii)(C)(I): an accessible route into and through the covered multifamily dwelling;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(4)(c)(ii)(C)(II): light switches, electrical outlets, thermostats, and other environmental controls in accessible locations;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(4)(c)(ii)(C)(III): reinforcements in the bathroom walls to allow later installation of grab bars; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(4)(c)(ii)(C)(IV): kitchens and bathrooms such that an individual in a wheelchair can maneuver about and use the space.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-5(5): This section also applies to discriminatory housing practices because of race, color, religion, sex, national origin, familial status, source of income, disability, sexual orientation, or gender identity based upon a person's association with another person.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-6 Discriminatory housing practices regarding residential real estate-related transactions -- Discriminatory housing practices regarding the provisions of brokerage services.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-6(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-6(1)(a): It is a discriminatory housing practice for a person whose business includes engaging in residential real estate-related transactions to discriminate against a person in making available a residential real estate-related transaction, or in the terms or conditions of the residential real estate-related transaction, because of race, color, religion, sex, disability, familial status, source of income, national origin, sexual orientation, or gender identity.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-6(1)(b): Residential real estate-related transactions include:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-6(1)(b)(i): making or purchasing loans or providing other financial assistance:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-6(1)(b)(i)(A): for purchasing, constructing, improving, repairing, or maintaining a dwelling; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-6(1)(b)(i)(B): secured by residential real estate; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-6(1)(b)(ii): selling, brokering, or appraising residential real property.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-6(2): It is a discriminatory housing practice to, because of race, color, religion, sex, disability, familial status, source of income, national origin, sexual orientation, or gender identity:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-6(2)(a): deny a person access to, or membership or participation in, a multiple-listing service, real estate brokers' organization, or other service, organization, or facility relating to the business of selling or renting dwellings; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-6(2)(b): discriminate against a person in the terms or conditions of access, membership, or participation in the organization, service, or facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-6(3): This section also applies to a discriminatory housing practice because of race, color, religion, sex, national origin, familial status, source of income, disability, sexual orientation, or gender identity based upon a person's association with another person.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-7 Prohibited conduct -- Aiding or abetting in discriminatory actions -- Obstruction of division investigation -- Reprisals.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-7(1): It is a discriminatory housing practice to do any of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-7(1)(a): coerce, intimidate, threaten, or interfere with a person:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-7(1)(a)(i): in the exercise or enjoyment of a right granted or protected under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-7(1)(a)(ii): because that person exercised a right granted or protected under this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-7(1)(a)(iii): because that person aided or encouraged any other person in the exercise or enjoyment of a right granted or protected under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-7(1)(b): aid, abet, incite, compel, or coerce a person to engage in a practice prohibited by this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-7(1)(c): attempt to aid, abet, incite, compel, or coerce a person to engage in a practice prohibited by this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-7(1)(d): obstruct or prevent a person from complying with this chapter, or any order issued under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-7(1)(e): resist, prevent, impede, or interfere with the director or a division employee or representative in the performance of duty under this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-7(1)(f): engage in a reprisal against a person because that person:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-7(1)(f)(i): opposed a practice prohibited under this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-7(1)(f)(ii): filed a complaint, testified, assisted, or participated in any manner in an investigation, proceeding, or hearing under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-7(2): This section also applies to discriminatory housing practices because of race, color, religion, sex, national origin, familial status, source of income, disability, sexual orientation, or gender identity based upon a person's association with another person.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-8 Jurisdiction -- Commission -- Division.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-8(1): The commission has jurisdiction over the subject of housing discrimination under this chapter and may delegate the responsibility of receiving, processing, and investigating allegations of discriminatory housing practices and enforcing this chapter to the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-8(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The commission may:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-8(2)(a): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-8(2)(b): appoint and prescribe the duties of investigators, legal counsel, and other employees and agents that it considers necessary for the enforcement of this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-8(2)(c): issue subpoenas to compel the attendance of witnesses or the production of evidence for use in any investigation, conference, or hearing conducted by the division, and if a person fails to comply with a subpoena, petition a court of competent jurisdiction for an order to show cause why that person should not be held in contempt.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-8(3): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act The division:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-8(3)(a): may receive, reject, investigate, and determine complaints alleging discriminatory housing practices prohibited by this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-8(3)(b): shall attempt conciliation between the parties through informal efforts, conference, persuasion, or other reasonable methods for the purposes of resolving the complaint;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-8(3)(c): may seek prompt judicial action for appropriate temporary or preliminary relief pending final disposition of a complaint if the division and the commission conclude that an action is necessary to carry out the purposes of this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-8(3)(d): may, with the commission, initiate a civil action in a court of competent jurisdiction to:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-8(3)(d)(i): enforce the rights granted or protected under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-8(3)(d)(ii): seek injunctive or other equitable relief, including temporary restraining orders, preliminary injunctions, or permanent injunctions;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-8(3)(d)(iii): seek damages;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-8(3)(d)(iv): enforce final commission orders on the division's own behalf or on behalf of another person in order to carry out the purposes of this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-8(3)(d)(v): enforce the terms of a conciliation agreement in the event of a breach;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-8(3)(e): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act may initiate formal agency action under
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-8(3)(f): may promote public awareness of the rights and remedies under this chapter by implementing programs to increase the awareness of landlords, real estate agents, and other citizens of their rights and responsibilities under the Utah Fair Housing Act, but may not solicit fair housing complaints or cases.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9 Procedure for an aggrieved person to file a complaint -- Conciliation -- Investigation -- Determination.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(1): An aggrieved person may file a written verified complaint with the division within 180 days after the day on which an alleged discriminatory housing practice occurs.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(2)(a): The commission shall adopt rules consistent with 24 C.F.R. Sec. 115.3 (1990), relating to procedures under related federal law, to govern:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(2)(a)(i): the form of the complaint;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(2)(a)(ii): the form of any answer to the complaint;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(2)(a)(iii): procedures for filing or amending a complaint or answer; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(2)(a)(iv): the form of notice to a party accused of the act or omission giving rise to the complaint.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(2)(b): The commission may, by rule, prescribe any other procedure pertaining to the division's processing of the complaint.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(3): During the period beginning with the filing of the complaint and ending with the director's determination, the division shall, to the extent feasible, engage in conciliation with respect to the complaint.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(4)(a): The division shall commence proceedings to investigate and conciliate a complaint alleging a discriminatory housing practice within 30 days after the day on which the complainant files the complaint.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(4)(b): After the commencement of an investigation, any party may request that the commission review the proceedings to ensure compliance with the requirements of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(5)(a): The division shall complete the investigation within 100 days after the day on which the complainant files the complaint, unless it is impracticable to do so.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(5)(b): If the division is unable to complete the investigation within 100 days after the day on which the complainant files the complaint, the division shall notify the complainant and respondent in writing of the reasons for the delay.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(6): If, as a result of the division's investigation, the director determines that there is no reasonable cause to support an allegation in the complaint, the director shall issue a written determination dismissing the complaint.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(7): (7)(a)(i); (7)(a); 57-21-11 If, as a result of the division's investigation of a complaint, the director determines that there is reasonable cause to support an allegation in the complaint:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(7)(a): (7)(a)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(7)(a)(i): the division shall informally endeavor to eliminate or correct the discriminatory housing practice through a conciliation conference between the parties, presided over by the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(7)(a)(ii): (7)(a)(i) nothing said or done in the course of a conciliation conference described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(7)(b): (7)(a); 57-21-11
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(7)(b)(i): (7)(a) if the conciliation conference described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(7)(b)(i)(A): the parties shall execute a conciliation agreement, approved by the division, setting forth the resolution of the issues; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(7)(b)(i)(B): the parties or the division may enforce the conciliation agreement in an action filed in a court of competent jurisdiction; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-9(7)(b)(ii): 57-21-11 if the division is unable to obtain a conciliation agreement, the director shall issue a written determination stating the director's findings and ordering appropriate relief under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-13 Disclosure of information.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-13(1): Conciliation agreements and the director's determination and order are public records.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-13(2): (3) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-13(2)(a): Information used by the director in making any determination may be provided to all interested parties for the purpose of preparation for and participation in the investigation and any proceedings before the commission or court.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-13(2)(b): General statistical information may be disclosed provided identities of individuals or parties are not disclosed.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-13(2)(c): Information may be disclosed for inspection upon proper request by the attorney general or other legal representatives of the state or commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-13(2)(d): Information may be disclosed for information and reporting requirements of the federal government.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-13(3): The commission or its staff may not divulge or make public any information gained from any investigation, settlement negotiation, conciliation, hearing, or administrative proceeding before the commission if a privacy interest entitled to protection by law exists or the commission determines that disclosure will not further the purposes of this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-21-14 Effect of federal action.
--------------------------------------------------------
The commencement of an action in a federal court of competent jurisdiction for relief under federal law based upon any act prohibited by this chapter bars the commencement or continuation of any adjudicative proceeding before the division or state court proceeding in connection with the same claims under this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 57 - Chapter 22 - Utah Fit Premises Act
*******************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-1 Short title.
------------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Utah Fit Premises Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-2 Definitions.
------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-2(1): "Owner" means the owner, lessor, or sublessor of a residential rental unit.  A managing agent, leasing agent, or resident manager is considered an owner for purposes of notice and other communication required or allowed under this chapter unless the agent or manager specifies otherwise in writing in the rental agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-2(2): "Rental agreement" means any agreement, written or oral, which establishes or modifies the terms, conditions, rules, or any other provisions regarding the use and occupancy of a residential rental unit.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-2(3): "Rental application" means an application required by an owner as a prerequisite to the owner entering into a rental agreement for a residential rental unit.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-2(4): "Renter" means any person entitled under a rental agreement to occupy a residential rental unit to the exclusion of others.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-2(5): "Residential rental unit" means a renter's principal place of residence and includes the appurtenances, grounds, and facilities held out for the use of the residential renter generally, and any other area or facility provided to the renter in the rental agreement.  It does not include facilities contained in a boarding or rooming house or similar facility, mobile home lot, or recreational property rented on an occasional basis.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-3 Duties of owners and renters -- Generally.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-3(1): Each owner and his agent renting or leasing a residential rental unit shall maintain that unit in a condition fit for human habitation and in accordance with local ordinances and the rules of the board of health having jurisdiction in the area in which the residential rental unit is located.  Each residential rental unit shall have electrical systems, heating, plumbing, and hot and cold water.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-3(2): Each renter shall cooperate in maintaining his residential rental unit in accordance with this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-3(3): This chapter does not apply to breakage, malfunctions, or other conditions which do not materially affect the physical health or safety of the ordinary renter.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-3(4): Any duty in this act may be allocated to a different party by explicit written agreement signed by the parties.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4 Owner's duties.
---------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(1): To protect the physical health and safety of the ordinary renter, an owner:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(1)(a): may not rent the premises unless they are safe, sanitary, and fit for human occupancy; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(1)(b): shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(1)(b)(i): maintain common areas of the residential rental unit in a sanitary and safe condition;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(1)(b)(ii): maintain electrical systems, plumbing, heating, and hot and cold water;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(1)(b)(iii): maintain any air conditioning system in an operable condition;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(1)(b)(iv): maintain other appliances and facilities as specifically contracted in the rental agreement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(1)(b)(v): for buildings containing more than two residential rental units, provide and maintain appropriate receptacles for garbage and other waste and arrange for its removal, except to the extent that the renter and owner otherwise agree.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(2): Except as otherwise provided in the rental agreement, an owner shall provide the renter at least 24 hours prior notice of the owner's entry into the renter's residential rental unit.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(3): (4); (3)(a)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(3)(a): (4) Before an owner accepts an application fee or any other payment from a prospective renter, the owner shall disclose in writing to the prospective renter:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(3)(a)(i): a good faith estimate of:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(3)(a)(i)(A): the rent amount; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(3)(a)(i)(B): the amount of each fixed, non-rent expense that is part of the rental agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(3)(a)(ii): the type of each use-based, non-rent expense that is part of the rental agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(3)(a)(iii): the day on which the residential rental unit is scheduled to be available;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(3)(a)(iv): the criteria that the owner will consider in determining the prospective renter's eligibility as a renter in the residential rental unit, including criteria related to the prospective renter's criminal history, credit, income, employment, or rental history; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(3)(a)(v): (4) the requirements and process for the prospective renter to recover money the prospective renter pays in relation to the residential rental unit, as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(3)(b): (3)(a)(i) An owner may satisfy the written disclosure requirement described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(4): (3); (3); (4)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(4)(a): (3); (3) A prospective renter may make a written demand to the owner of a residential rental unit requesting the return of money the prospective renter paid in relation to the rental of the residential rental unit, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(4)(a)(i): (3); (3)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(4)(a)(i)(A): (3) an amount the owner provides in the good-faith estimate described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(4)(a)(i)(B): (3) the rental agreement includes a type of use-based, non-rent expense that was not disclosed under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(4)(a)(ii): the prospective renter:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(4)(a)(ii)(A): makes the written demand within five business days after the day on which the prospective renter receives the rental agreement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(4)(a)(ii)(B): at the time the prospective renter makes the written demand, has not signed the rental agreement or taken possession of the residential rental unit.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(4)(b): (4)(a) If a prospective renter makes a written demand in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(5): An owner may not charge a renter:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(5)(a): a late fee that exceeds the greater of:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(5)(a)(i): 10% of the rent agreed to in the rental agreement; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(5)(a)(ii): $75; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(5)(b): a fee, fine, assessment, interest, or other cost:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(5)(b)(i): in an amount greater than the amount agreed to in the rental agreement; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(5)(b)(ii): that is not included in the rental agreement, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(5)(b)(ii)(A): the rental agreement is on a month-to-month basis; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(5)(b)(ii)(B): the owner provides the renter a 15-day notice of the charge.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(6): Before an owner and a prospective renter enter into a rental agreement, the owner shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(6)(a): provide the prospective renter a written inventory of the condition of the residential rental unit, excluding ordinary wear and tear;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(6)(b): furnish the renter a form to document the condition of the residential rental unit and then allow the resident a reasonable time after the renter's occupancy of the residential rental unit to complete and return the form; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(6)(c): provide the prospective renter an opportunity to conduct a walkthrough inspection of the residential rental unit.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(7): At or before the commencement of the rental term under a rental agreement, an owner shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(7)(a): disclose in writing to the renter:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(7)(a)(i): the owner's name, address, and telephone number; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(7)(a)(ii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(7)(a)(ii)(A): the name, address, and telephone number of any person authorized to manage the residential rental unit; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(7)(a)(ii)(B): the name, address, and telephone number of any person authorized to act for and on behalf of the owner for purposes of receiving notice under this chapter or performing the owner's duties under this chapter or under the rental agreement, if the person authorized to manage the residential rental unit does not have authority to receive notice under this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(7)(b): provide the renter:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(7)(b)(i): an executed copy of the rental agreement, if the rental agreement is a written agreement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(7)(b)(ii): a copy of any rules and regulations applicable to the residential rental unit.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4(8): Nothing in this section prohibits any fee, fine, assessment, interest, or cost that is allowed by law or stated in the rental agreement.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4.1 Failure to deliver possession of residential rental unit -- Renter's option to terminate rental agreement -- Abatement of rent.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4.1(1): If an owner fails to deliver possession of a residential rental unit on the date provided in the rental agreement:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4.1(1)(a): the renter may, by written notice to the owner, terminate the rental agreement; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4.1(1)(b): if the renter chooses not to terminate the rental agreement, rent abates until the owner delivers possession as provided in the rental agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-4.1(2): (1)(a) If a renter terminates a rental agreement under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-5 Renter's duties -- Cleanliness and sanitation -- Compliance with written agreement -- Destruction of property, interference with peaceful enjoyment prohibited.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-5(1): Each renter shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-5(1)(a): comply with the rules of the board of health having jurisdiction in the area in which the residential rental unit is located which materially affect physical health and safety;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-5(1)(b): maintain the premises occupied in a clean and safe condition and shall not unreasonably burden any common area;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-5(1)(c): dispose of all garbage and other waste in a clean and safe manner;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-5(1)(d): maintain all plumbing fixtures in as sanitary a condition as the fixtures permit;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-5(1)(e): use all electrical, plumbing, sanitary, heating, and other facilities and appliances in a reasonable manner;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-5(1)(f): occupy the residential rental unit in the manner for which it was designed, but the renter may not increase the number of occupants above that specified in the rental agreement without written permission of the owner;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-5(1)(g): be current on all payments required by the rental agreement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-5(1)(h): comply with each rule, regulation, or requirement of the rental agreement, including any prohibition on, or the allowance of, smoking tobacco products within the residential rental unit, or on the premises, or both.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-5(2): A renter may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-5(2)(a): intentionally or negligently destroy, deface, damage, impair, or remove any part of the residential rental unit or knowingly permit any person to do so;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-5(2)(b): interfere with the peaceful enjoyment of the residential rental unit of another renter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-22-5(2)(c): unreasonably deny access to, refuse entry to, or withhold consent to enter the residential rental unit to the owner, agent, or manager for the purpose of making repairs to the unit.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 57 - Chapter 23 - Real Estate Cooperative Marketing Act
***********************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-1 Short title.
------------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Real Estate Cooperative Marketing Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-2 Definitions.
------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-2(1): "Cooperative" means a form of coownership of real estate in which:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-2(1)(a): the fee interest in the real estate is held by a corporation, partnership, trust, or other legal entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-2(1)(b): an individual's interest in the cooperative is evidenced in a form such as stock, participation shares, membership certificates, or similar instrument; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-2(1)(c): the participating individual's right of occupancy is demonstrated by a proprietary lease or similar instrument.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-2(2): "Division" means the Division of Real Estate of the Department of Commerce.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-3 Administration by division.
---------------------------------------------------------
This chapter shall be administered by the Division of Real Estate.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-4 Exclusions.
-----------------------------------------
This chapter does not apply to:Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-4(1): Title 57, Chapter 19, Timeshare and Camp Resort Act an interest in real estate regulated under
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-4(2): Title 61, Chapter 1, Utah Uniform Securities Act an offering for an interest in real estate which is regulated under:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-4(2)(a): Title 61, Chapter 1, Utah Uniform Securities Act
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-4(2)(b): the securities laws of any state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-4(2)(c): federal securities laws; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-4(3): Title 58, Chapter 56, Building Inspector and Factory Built Housing Licensing Act a sale of manufactured housing licensed under


Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-5 License required.
-----------------------------------------------
Except as provided by Section

Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-6 Disclosure required.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-6(1): An individual may not offer, sell, or otherwise dispose of a cooperative interest in this state without making oral and written disclosure to the prospective purchaser regarding:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-6(1)(a): the actual property interest being sold;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-6(1)(b): the actual right of occupancy associated with that property interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-6(1)(c): any encumbrance to which the property interest is subject; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-6(1)(d): the terms of any financing, refinancing, prior sale, resale, or loan assumption to which the property interest is subject.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-6(2): (1) The disclosure required under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-7 Investigatory powers and proceedings of division.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-7(1): The division may:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-7(1)(a): make necessary public or private investigations within or outside of this state to determine whether any person has violated or is about to violate this chapter or any rule or order made by the division under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-7(1)(b): require or permit any person to file a statement in writing, under oath or otherwise as the division determines, as to all the facts and circumstances concerning the matter to be investigated.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-7(2): For the purpose of any investigation or proceeding under this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-7(2)(a): the division may administer oaths or affirmations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-7(2)(b): upon its own motion or upon the request of any party, the division may:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-7(2)(b)(i): subpoena witnesses;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-7(2)(b)(ii): compel their attendance;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-7(2)(b)(iii): take evidence; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-7(2)(b)(iv): require the production of any matter which is relevant to the investigation, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-7(2)(b)(iv)(A): the existence, description, nature, custody, condition and location of any books, documents, or other tangible records;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-7(2)(b)(iv)(B): the identity and location of persons having knowledge of relevant facts; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-7(2)(b)(iv)(C): any other matter reasonably calculated to lead to the discovery of material evidence.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-7(3): Upon failure of any person to obey a subpoena or to answer questions propounded by the investigating officer and upon reasonable notice to all persons affected by the subpoena or information sought to be discovered under the subpoena, the division may apply to the district court for an order compelling compliance.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-9 Voidable agreements.
--------------------------------------------------
Any agreement to purchase an interest in a real estate cooperative entered into in violation of this chapter may, at the option of the purchaser, be voided and the purchaser's entire consideration paid together with interest at the legal rate, any costs, and reasonable attorney's fees shall be recovered.  However, no suit under this section may be brought more than two years after:Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-9(1): the date the agreement is signed; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-9(2): the date the purchaser knew or reasonably should have known of the violation.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-10 Prosecution -- Penalties.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-10(1): The director may refer any available evidence concerning violations of this chapter or of any rule or order under this chapter to the attorney general or the appropriate prosecuting attorney, who may, in turn, institute the appropriate civil or criminal proceedings under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-10(2): Any person who willfully violates any provision of this chapter is guilty of a class B misdemeanor.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-10(3): Title 13, Chapter 11, Utah Consumer Sales Practices Act For purposes of applying
Utah Code Annotated § 57-23-10(4): The remedies provided in this chapter are cumulative and nonexclusive, and do not affect any other remedy available at law.

Utah Code Annotated § 57-24-102 Restriction on prohibition of display of flag.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-24-102(1): A residential property management authority may not prohibit a resident from displaying a flag:

Utah Code Annotated § 57-24-102(1)(c): from a staff, pole, or window.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-24-102(2): In any action to enforce this section, the prevailing party shall be awarded costs and reasonable attorney fees.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-24-102(3): This section does not apply to a contract or agreement entered into before May 3, 2004.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 57 - Chapter 25 - Uniform Environmental Covenants Act
*********************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-101 Title -- Scope.
-----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-101(1): This chapter is known as the "Uniform Environmental Covenants Act."
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-101(2): Title 19, Chapter 10, Environmental Institutional Control Act
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-101(2)(a): This chapter applies to an environmental covenant created on or after May 1, 2006.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-101(2)(b): Title 19, Chapter 10, Environmental Institutional Control Act
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-101(3): Title 19, Chapter 10, Environmental Institutional Control Act; 19-10-102 For the purposes of this chapter and


Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-102(1): "Activity and use limitations" means restrictions or obligations created under this chapter with respect to real property.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-102(2): "Agency" means the Utah Department of Environmental Quality or other state or federal agency that determines or approves the environmental response project under which the environmental covenant is created.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-102(3): "Common interest community" means a condominium, cooperative, or other real property with respect to which a person, by virtue of the person's ownership of a parcel of real property, is obligated to pay property taxes or insurance premiums, or for maintenance, or improvement of other real property described in a recorded covenant that creates the common interest community.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-102(4): "Environmental covenant" means a servitude arising under an environmental response project that imposes activity and use limitations.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-102(5): Title 19, Environmental Quality Code; Title 19, Chapter 8, Voluntary Cleanup Program "Environmental response project" means a plan, risk assessment, or work performed for environmental remediation of real property or surface and groundwater on or beneath the real property and conducted:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-102(5)(a): Title 19, Environmental Quality Code under a federal or state program governing environmental remediation of real property, including under
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-102(5)(b): incident to closure of a solid or hazardous waste management unit, if the closure is conducted with approval of an agency; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-102(5)(c): Title 19, Chapter 8, Voluntary Cleanup Program under the state voluntary clean-up program authorized in
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-102(6): 57-25-103(1) "Holder" means the grantee of an environmental covenant as specified in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-102(7): "Jurisdiction" means a state of the United States, the District of Columbia, Puerto Rico, the United States Virgin Islands, or any territory or insular possession subject to the jurisdiction of the United States.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-102(8): "Record," used as a noun, means information that is inscribed on a tangible medium or that is stored in an electronic or other medium and is retrievable in perceivable form.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-103 Nature of rights -- Subordination of interests.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-103(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-103(1)(a): Any person, including a person that owns an interest in the real property, the agency, or a municipality or other unit of local government, may be a holder.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-103(1)(b): An environmental covenant may identify more than one holder.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-103(1)(c): The interest of a holder is an interest in real property.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-103(2): A right of an agency under this chapter or under an environmental covenant, other than a right as a holder, is not an interest in real property.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-103(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-103(3)(a): An agency is bound by any obligation it affirmatively assumes in an environmental covenant, but an agency does not assume obligations merely by signing an environmental covenant.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-103(3)(b): Any other person that signs an environmental covenant is bound by the obligations the person assumes in the covenant, but signing the covenant does not change obligations, rights, or protections granted or imposed under law other than this chapter except as provided in the covenant.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-103(4): The following requirements apply to interests in real property in existence at the time an environmental covenant is created or amended:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-103(4)(a): An interest that has priority under other law is not affected by an environmental covenant unless the person that owns the interest subordinates that interest to the covenant.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-103(4)(b): This chapter does not require a person that owns a prior interest to subordinate that interest to an environmental covenant or to agree to be bound by the covenant.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-103(4)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-103(4)(c)(i): A subordination agreement may be contained in an environmental covenant covering real property or in a separate record.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-103(4)(c)(ii): If the environmental covenant covers commonly owned property in a common interest community, the record may be signed by any person authorized by the governing board of the owners' association.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-103(4)(d): An agreement by a person to subordinate a prior interest to an environmental covenant affects the priority of that person's interest but does not by itself impose any affirmative obligation on the person with respect to the environmental covenant.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104 Contents of environmental covenant.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104(1): An environmental covenant must:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104(1)(a): state that the instrument is an environmental covenant executed under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104(1)(b): contain a legally sufficient description of the real property subject to the covenant;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104(1)(c): describe the activity and use limitations on the real property;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104(1)(d): identify every holder;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104(1)(e): be signed by the agency, every holder, and unless waived by the agency, every owner of the fee simple of the real property subject to the covenant; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104(1)(f): identify the name and location of any administrative record for the environmental response project reflected in the environmental covenant.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104(2): (1); 57-25-109; 57-25-110; 57-25-111 In addition to the information required by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104(2)(a): requirements for notice following transfer of a specified interest in, or concerning proposed changes in use of, applications for building permits for, or proposals for any site work affecting the contamination on, the property subject to the covenant;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104(2)(b): requirements for periodic reporting describing compliance with the covenant;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104(2)(c): rights of access to the property granted in connection with implementation or enforcement of the covenant;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104(2)(d): a brief narrative description of the contamination and remedy, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104(2)(d)(i): the contaminants of concern;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104(2)(d)(ii): the pathways of exposure;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104(2)(d)(iii): limits on exposure; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104(2)(d)(iv): the location and extent of the contamination;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104(2)(e): 57-25-109; 57-25-110 limitation on amendment or termination of the covenant in addition to those contained in Sections

Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-104(3): In addition to other conditions for its approval of an environmental covenant, the agency may require those persons specified by the agency who have interests in the real property to sign the covenant.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-105 Validity -- Effect on other instruments.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-105(1): An environmental covenant that complies with this chapter runs with the land.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-105(2): An environmental covenant that is otherwise effective is valid and enforceable even if:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-105(2)(a): it is not appurtenant to an interest in real property;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-105(2)(b): it can be or has been assigned to a person other than the original holder;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-105(2)(c): it is not of a character that has been recognized traditionally at common law;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-105(2)(d): it imposes a negative burden;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-105(2)(e): it imposes an affirmative obligation on a person having an interest in the real property or on the holder;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-105(2)(f): the benefit or burden does not touch or concern real property;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-105(2)(g): there is no privity of estate or contract;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-105(2)(h): the holder dies, ceases to exist, resigns, or is replaced; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-105(2)(i): the owner of an interest subject to the environmental covenant and the holder are the same person.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-105(3): (2); (3)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-105(3)(a): (2) An instrument that creates restrictions or obligations with respect to real property that would qualify as activity and use limitations except for the fact that the instrument was recorded before the effective date of this chapter is not invalid or unenforceable because of any of the limitations on enforcement of interests described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-105(3)(b): (3)(a) This chapter does not apply in any other respect to an instrument covered under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-105(4): This chapter does not invalidate or render unenforceable any interest, whether designated as an environmental covenant or other interest, that is otherwise enforceable under Utah law.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-106 Relationship to other land use law.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-106(1): This chapter does not authorize a use of real property that is otherwise prohibited by:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-106(1)(a): a zoning law;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-106(1)(b): law other than this chapter regulating use of real property; or
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-106(1)(c): a recorded instrument that has priority over the environmental covenant.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-106(2): An environmental covenant may prohibit or restrict uses of real property that are authorized by zoning or by law other than this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-107 Notice.
---------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-107(1): A copy of an environmental covenant shall be provided by the persons and in the manner required by the agency to:
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-107(1)(a): each person that signed the covenant;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-107(1)(b): each person holding a recorded interest in the real property subject to the covenant;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-107(1)(c): each person in possession of the real property subject to the covenant;
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-107(1)(d): each municipality or other unit of local government in which real property subject to the covenant is located; and
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-107(1)(e): any other person that the agency requires.
Utah Code Annotated § 57-25-107(2): The validity of a covenant is not affected by failure to provide a copy of the covenant as required under this section.
